Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
12 min
Waqf During Terminal Illness: Treated as a Bequest, Limited to One-Third
Outlining the rules for waqf made during terminal illness, treated as a bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for waqf made during terminal illness and differentiate between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding bindingness and the one-third limit.

Core Idea
A waqf during terminal illness is like a will, so it only binds one-third without heir consent.

Waqf is normally irrevocable and can be made from all one's property, but when made during a terminal illness, it is treated like a bequest (wasiyyah). This means it is limited to one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on whether such a waqf is binding at all, but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) follows the Sahibayn: it is binding but restricted to one-third.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
Recognize that a waqf made during marad al-mawt is treated as a bequest, not a normal waqf. This changes the scope and bindingness.
2
State the ruling on the one-third limit
The waqf is valid from up to one-third of the estate. Any excess is invalid unless all heirs consent. This is agreed upon by Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, though they differ on bindingness.
In health, waqf is from the entire wealth.
3
Note the intra-madhhab difference on bindingness
Abu Hanifa holds that waqf in illness is not binding (revocable), while the Sahibayn hold it is binding. The fatwa follows the Sahibayn's view.
The source cites al-Tahawi and al-Hidayah for this.
4
Apply the ruling to the examples given
Work through the woman's case: waqf on daughters and descendants, with a contesting sister. Only one-third valid; yield of that one-third shared among all heirs during daughters' lifetimes. Then the man with only daughters: one-third immediate, two-thirds require their ratification.
Also note the principle: a bequest to an heir is invalid if there are other contesting heirs.
5
Understand the rationale
The ma'na (underlying reason) is that the waqf is like a will, and a will cannot exceed one-third without consent. The restriction protects inheritance rights of other heirs.
This is based on the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas: 'One-third is much, and to leave your heirs rich is better.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الهداية ولو وقف في مرض موته قال الطحاوي : هو بمنزلة الوصية بعد الموت والصحيح أنه لا يلزم عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يلزم إلا أنه يعتبر من الثلث والوقف في الصحة من جميع المال .اهـ. وفي الظهيرية: امرأة وقفت منزلاً في مرضها على بناتها ثم من بعدهن على أولادهن وأولاد أولادهن أبداً ما تناسلوا فإذا انقرضوا فللفقراء ثم ماتت من مرضها وخلفت من الورثة بنتين وأختاً لأب والأخت لا ترضى بما صنعت ولا مال لها سوى المنزل، جاز الوقف في الثلث ولم يجز في الثلثين فيقسم الثلثان بين الورثة على قدر سهامهم ويوقف الثلث، فما خرج من غلته قسم بين الورثة كلهم على قدر سهامهم ما عاشت البنتان فإذا ماتتا صرفت الغلة إلى أولادهما وأولاد أولادهما كما شرطت الواقفة لا حق للورثة في ذلك رجل وقف داراً له في مرضه على ثلاث بنات له وليس له وارث غيرهن قال الثلث من الدار وقف والثلثان مطلق له يصنعن بهما ما شئن . قال الفقيه أبو الليث هذا إذا لم يجزن، أما إذا أجزن صار الكل وقفاً عليهن اهـ. والحاصل أن المريض إذا وقف على بعض ورثته ثم من بعدهم على أولادهم ثم على الفقراء، فإن أجاز الوارث الآخر كان الكل وقفاً واتبع الشرط وإلا كان الثلثان ملكاً بين الورثة والثلث وقفاً مع أن الوصية للبعض لا تنفذ في شيء لأنه لم يتمحض للوارث لأنه بعده لغيره فاعتبر الغير بالنظر إلى الثلث، واعتبر الوارث بالنظر إلى غلة الثلث الذي صار وقفاً فلا يتبع الشرط ما دام الوارث حياً، وإنما تقسم غلة هذا الثلث بين الورثة على فرائض الله تعالى، فإذا انقرض الوارث الموقوف عليه اعتبر شرطه في غلة الثلث. وإن وقف على غير الورثة ولم يجيزوا كان . القضاة قد قضى بلزوم هذا الوقف وبطلان حق الرجوع ليس بشيء في الصحيح؛ كذا في الكافي والخانية اهـ . قوله : (قال الثلث من الدار وقف الخ) أي لأن الوقف في المرض وصية فتنفذ الثلث من فقط إلا بإجازة لكن صرحوا بأن الوصية للوارث لا تجوز ولعل مرادهم أنها لا تجوز حيث وجد المنازع وهو الوارث الآخر لتعلق حقه، أما إذا لم يوجد وارث غير الموصى له فتجوز بلا إجازة لعدم المنازع لكن قد يقال : إذا لم يوجد غيره فلم لا تجوز في الكل بل توقف جوازها في الثلثين على الإحازة. وقد يجاب بأن الشارع لم يجعل للموصي حقاً فيما زاد على الثلث فلم تجز في الزائد وإن
In al-Hidaya: If one makes a waqf during his terminal illness, al-Tahawi said: It is like a bequest after death. The correct view is that it is not binding according to Abu Hanifa, while it is binding according to the two disciples but it is considered from the one-third, whereas waqf in health is from the entire wealth. End. In al-Zahiriyya: A woman made a waqf of a house during her illness upon her daughters, then after them upon their children and grandchildren forever as long as they multiply, then when extinct for the poor. Then she died of that illness, leaving as heirs two daughters and a paternal sister. The sister does not approve of what she did, and she has no wealth other than the house. The waqf is valid for one-third and invalid for two-thirds. So the two-thirds is divided among the heirs according to their shares, and the one-third is held in waqf. Whatever yield comes from it is divided among all the heirs according to their shares as long as the two daughters are alive. When they die, the yield is given to their children and grandchildren as the waqif stipulated; the heirs have no right in that. [Another case:] A man made a waqf of a house during his illness upon his three daughters, and he has no other heir. He said: One-third of the house is waqf, and two-thirds are free, they may do whatever they wish with them. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: This is if they do not ratify; if they ratify, the entirety becomes waqf upon them. End. The summary: If a sick person makes a waqf upon some of his heirs, then after them upon their children, then upon the poor, then if the other heir ratifies, the whole becomes waqf and the condition is followed. Otherwise, two-thirds is owned by the heirs and one-third is waqf, even though a bequest to a part [heir] does not execute at all because it is not exclusively for an heir (since after him it is for others). So consideration is given to the others in respect to the corpus of the one-third, and to the heir in respect to the yield of that one-third which became waqf. Hence the condition is not followed as long as the heir is alive, and the yield of this one-third is divided among the heirs according to the shares of Allah. When the heir on whom the waqf was made dies, his condition is considered in the yield of the one-third. If [the sick person] made a waqf on non-heirs and they did not ratify, it is... The judges have ruled on the bindingness of this waqf and the nullity of the right of revocation; that is not valid in the correct view; thus in al-Kafi and al-Khaniyya. End. His statement: (He said: One-third of the house is waqf etc.) meaning because the waqf during illness is a bequest, so it is executed only from one-third unless permission is given. But they explicitly stated that a bequest to an heir is not permissible. Perhaps they mean it is not permissible when there is a contestant, i.e., another heir whose right is attached. If there is no heir besides the legatee, then it is permissible without permission because there is no contestant. But it may be said: If there is no other, why is it not permissible in the whole? Rather, its permissibility in the two-thirds depends on ratification. It may be answered that the Lawgiver did not give the testator the right to exceed one-third, so it is not permissible in the excess, and...
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage covers the rulings for waqf made during a terminal illness (marad al-mawt). The key principle is that such a waqf is treated like a wasiyyah (bequest) and thus is limited to one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent. According to Abu Hanifa, waqf during illness is not binding (non-revocable) at all, while according to the two disciples it is binding but considers the one-third limit. The text provides a detailed example: a woman endows her house on her daughters and their descendants, then for the poor. Upon her death, the heirs include two daughters and a paternal sister. Since the sister does not ratify, only one-third is valid as waqf; the remaining two-thirds goes to the heirs. The yield of the one-third is shared among all heirs during the daughters' lifetimes, and only after their death does it go to the specified descendents. Another example involves a man with only three daughters who makes a waqf on them—the one-third is immediately effective, the two-thirds only if the daughters ratify. The commentary then clarifies that a bequest to an heir is generally invalid, but if there is no contesting heir, it may be valid without ratification. The final note corrects a misconception: a judge's ruling making such a waqf binding does not affect the correct ruling that the right of revocation is null in the valid view.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A terminal illness from which death is expected and which eventually leads to death.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will that takes effect after death, limited to one-third of the estate without heir consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example from al-Zahiriyya of the woman who made a waqf of her house upon her daughters and descendants, with the sister as a contesting heir, what happens to the yield (income) of the one-third waqf portion during the lifetimes of the two daughters?
A) It goes entirely to the daughters.
B) It is divided among all the heirs (daughters and sister) according to their inheritance shares.
C) It is given to the poor.
D) It is accumulated for the descendants.

Key Takeaway
A waqf made during terminal illness is treated as a bequest and is thus limited to one-third of the estate unless all heirs consent to exceed it.

Waqf in Terminal Illness: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waqf in terminal illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the bindingness of a waqf made in terminal illness and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A waqf in terminal illness binds only from one-third; the dispute is about when it binds.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: does a waqf made during terminal illness become binding immediately or only after death? The source passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq shows the tarjih in favor of the Sahibayn, establishing the fatwa position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa says the waqf is not binding until death (like a will); the Sahibayn say it is binding immediately but limited to one-third.
Both agree on the one-third limitation; the dispute is on timing of binding.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opponent is Abu Hanifa himself within the school. His view is that the waqf is revocable until death.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The text does not explicitly cite Abu Hanifa's proof, but it implies qiyas on wasiyyah (will) which is not binding until death.
The Sahibayn's proof is a claimed continuous consensus (ijma mutawarith) from the Companions.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The later scholars (mashayikh) and the author of Fath al-Qadir give preponderance to the Sahibayn's view, considering it the truth and the basis for fatwa.
The phrase 'al-khulā yasur' may indicate a principle easing the application.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the waqf can be revoked any time before death; under Sahibayn, it is irrevocable immediately but only up to one-third.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view, so the immediate binding effect prevails in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحاصل أن المشايخ رجحوا قولهما وقال بالخلا يسر كذا الفتوى عليه. وفي فتح القدير: إنه الحق، ولا يبعد أن يكون إجماع الصحابة ومن مر بعدهم متوارثاً على خلاف قوله وفي الهداية ولو وقف في مرض موته قال الطحاوي : هو بمنزلة الوصية بعد الموت والصحيح أنه لا يلزم عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يلزم إلا أنه يعتبر من الثلث والوقف في الصحة من جميع المال .اهـ.
And the summary is that the scholars (mashayikh) preferred the view of the two (companions) and said: 'al-khulā yasur', thus the fatwa is upon it. And in Fath al-Qadir: it is the truth, and it is not far that it is a continuous consensus of the Companions and those after them contrary to his statement. And in al-Hidayah: 'And if he made a waqf in his terminal illness,' al-Tahawi said: 'It is like a will after death. The correct position is that it is not binding according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two (companions) it is binding, except that it is considered from the one-third, whereas a waqf during health is from the entire estate.'
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding waqf made during marad al-mawt (terminal illness). The author states that the later scholars (mashayikh) have given preponderance (tarjih) to the view of the two companions (Sahibayn) over Abu Hanifa's view. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that such a waqf is binding but only to the extent of one-third of the estate, analogous to a will (wasiyyah). The phrase 'al-khulā yasur' is ambiguous but likely refers to a principle that eases the strict rule. The author cites Fath al-Qadir, which argues that the consensus (ijma') of the Companions and later generations supports the Sahibayn. The text then quotes al-Hidayah: according to al-Tahawi, the correct view is that Abu Hanifa held such a waqf non-binding (la yalzam) until death, while the Sahibayn held it binding from the moment of declaration but limited to the one-third. In health, a waqf is valid from the entire estate without limit.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A terminal illness from which death is likely and occurs, making actions subject to will-like restrictions.
الثلث (al-thuluth): The one-third of the estate that can be disposed of by will or waqf in terminal illness without heir consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), a waqf made during terminal illness is binding from what portion of the estate?
A) From the entire estate without restriction
B) From one-third only, unless heirs consent to more
C) It is never binding until death
D) From one-half of the estate

Key Takeaway
A waqf in terminal illness is binding immediately but only up to one-third of the estate; this is the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Waqf in Terminal Illness on Heirs: The Case of Daughters and Descendants
Complete case study and derivation of a general rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a terminally ill person's waqf on heirs, apply the one-third limitation, and determine how the usufruct of the waqf is distributed among all heirs while the immediate beneficiaries are alive.

Core Idea
A terminally ill person's waqf on heirs is valid only within one-third of the estate; its usufruct is treated as inheritance among all heirs until the immediate beneficiaries die.

This lesson examines a detailed case from al-Zahiriyyah: a woman in her terminal illness makes a waqf of her house on her daughters (who are heirs) and then on their descendants, then the poor. She dies leaving two daughters and a paternal sister; the sister does not consent. The ruling clarifies the limits of such a waqf and the unique distribution of its revenue (ghullah) among all heirs. From this case, the author derives a general principle for waqf by a sick person on some heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key parties and the waqf structure
Name the waqif (the woman), the beneficiaries (daughters, then their descendants, then the poor), and the heirs at death (two daughters, paternal sister). Note the sister does not consent.
The waqf includes a cascade of beneficiaries, making it not exclusively for heirs.
2
Determine the limit on waqf in terminal illness
A terminally ill person's disposition is treated like a bequest: valid only in one-third of the estate without consent of other heirs. Here, the sister does not consent, so the waqf is valid only in one-third of the house.
This follows the general rule that a muslim's will is limited to one-third.
3
Apply faraid shares to the two-thirds inheritance
The remaining two-thirds are inherited by the three heirs: two daughters collectively receive 2/3 (fard), and the paternal sister receives 1/3 (as asabah ma'a al-banat). The shares are 2:1, so out of 3 shares, daughters get 2 and sister gets 1.
The base number is 3; no awl or radd needed.
4
Understand the distribution of the waqf's usufruct
The usufruct (ghullah) of the one-third waqf is not given exclusively to the daughters during their lifetimes. Instead, it is divided among all heirs (daughters and sister) according to their faraid shares. This continues as long as the daughters live.
The condition of the waqif is suspended while the immediate heir-beneficiary is alive; the usufruct is treated as inheritance.
5
State the general rule for waqf on some heirs
If a terminally ill person makes a waqf on some heirs, then on others (non-heirs), and other heirs do not consent, the waqf is valid in one-third. The usufruct of that one-third is distributed among all heirs according to inheritance shares until the immediate heir-beneficiaries die. After their death, the waqif's stipulation is followed.
This balances the rights of heirs and the intent of the waqif.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية: امرأة وقفت منزلاً في مرضها على بناتها ثم من بعدهن على أولادهن وأولاد أولادهن أبداً ما تناسلوا فإذا انقرضوا فللفقراء ثم ماتت من مرضها وخلفت من الورثة بنتين وأختاً لأب والأخت لا ترضى بما صنعت ولا مال لها سوى المنزل، جاز الوقف في الثلث ولم يجز في الثلثين فيقسم الثلثان بين الورثة على قدر سهامهم ويوقف الثلث، فما خرج من غلته قسم بين الورثة كلهم على قدر سهامهم ما عاشت البنتان فإذا ماتتا صرفت الغلة إلى أولادهما وأولاد أولادهما كما شرطت الواقفة لا حق للورثة في ذلك. والحاصل أن المريض إذا وقف على بعض ورثته ثم من بعدهم على أولادهم ثم على الفقراء، فإن أجاز الوارث الآخر كان الكل وقفاً واتبع الشرط وإلا كان الثلثان ملكاً بين الورثة والثلث وقفاً مع أن الوصية للبعض لا تنفذ في شيء لأنه لم يتمحض للوارث لأنه بعده لغيره فاعتبر الغير بالنظر إلى الثلث، واعتبر الوارث بالنظر إلى غلة الثلث الذي صار وقفاً فلا يتبع الشرط ما دام الوارث حياً، وإنما تقسم غلة هذا الثلث بين الورثة على فرائض الله تعالى، فإذا انقرض الوارث الموقوف عليه اعتبر شرطه في غلة الثلث. وإن وقف على غير الورثة ولم يجيزوا كان
And in al-Zahiriyyah: A woman made a waqf of a house during her illness upon her daughters, then after them upon their children and their children forever as long as they multiply, and when they become extinct then upon the poor. Then she died of that illness and left heirs: two daughters and a paternal sister. The sister does not agree with what she did, and she has no property besides the house. The waqf is valid in the one-third and not valid in the two-thirds. So the two-thirds are divided among the heirs according to their shares, and the one-third is stopped (as waqf). Whatever revenue comes from it is divided among all the heirs according to their shares as long as the two daughters are alive. When they die, the revenue is given to their children and their children's children as the waqif stipulated; the heirs have no right in that. And the summary is: When a sick person makes a waqf on some of his heirs, then after them upon their children, then upon the poor: if the other heir consents, the whole is waqf and the condition is followed; otherwise the two-thirds are property among the heirs and the one-third is waqf, even though a bequest to an heir does not execute at all. But here it is not exclusively for the heir because after him it is for others, so the other beneficiaries are considered with respect to the one-third, and the heir is considered with respect to the produce of the one-third that became waqf. So the condition is not followed as long as the heir is alive; rather, the produce of this one-third is divided among the heirs according to the divine shares. When the heir upon whom the waqf was made becomes extinct, his condition is followed regarding the produce of the one-third. And if he made a waqf on non-heirs and they did not consent...
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a detailed faraid-style case study and derives a general rule. The case: a woman in terminal illness makes a waqf of her only asset (a house) on her two daughters (who are heirs) and then on their descendants, then on the poor. She leaves two daughters and a paternal sister as heirs. The sister does not consent to the waqf. Ruling: The waqf is valid only in one-third of the house; the two-thirds remain as inheritance divided among all three heirs according to their shares (daughters: 2/3 each? Actually in faraid, daughters get 2/3 together, sister gets 1/3? Wait the shares: two daughters: 2/3 collectively (each 1/3), sister: 1/3? But the text says 'on the basis of their shares' (فرائض الله). The usufruct of the one-third is distributed among all heirs (including the sister) as long as the daughters are alive. After the daughters die, the usufruct goes to their descendants per the stipulation. The general rule derived: If a sick person makes a waqf on some heirs (e.g., daughters) and then on others (grandchildren), the one-third is waqf but the usufruct is treated as inheritance among all heirs while the immediate beneficiaries are alive. Only after they die does the stipulation take effect for the subsequent beneficiaries. If the waqf is on non-heirs, the same one-third rule applies but with different distribution.

Key Terms
الغلّة (al-ghullah): The revenue or usufruct generated by the waqf property (e.g., rent).
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness; a disease that usually leads to death and from which the person dies within a year without returning to health.
الوقف على الورثة (al-waqf 'ala al-warithah): Waqf where the immediate beneficiaries are heirs of the waqif.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of the woman who made a waqf on her daughters and their descendants, who receives the usufruct of the waqf while the daughters are alive?
A) Only the daughters
B) Only the poor
C) All the heirs (daughters and sister) as per inheritance shares
D) The daughters and their children

Key Takeaway
A terminally ill person's waqf on heirs is valid in one-third, and its usufruct is distributed among all heirs by inheritance shares during the heirs' lifetimes.

Waqf in Illness on Only Heirs: The One-Third Rule and Ijazah
Case ruling on waqf in illness on sole heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a waqf made during terminal illness when the beneficiaries are the only heirs, and explain the effect of their consent (ijazah).

Core Idea
A waqf in illness on one's only heirs is limited to one-third unless they consent after death.

This lesson examines a specific case: a man in his final illness makes a waqf of his house on his three daughters, who are his sole heirs. The ruling distinguishes between the part that becomes waqf automatically and the part that requires the heirs' approval. Understanding this illustrates a key principle of Islamic inheritance law: dispositions during terminal illness are restricted to one-third of the estate to protect heirs' rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
A man in marad al-mawt (terminal illness) makes a waqf of his house on his three daughters. They are his only heirs.
2
Determine the default ruling
One-third of the house becomes waqf automatically; the remaining two-thirds are owned absolutely by the daughters (they may do as they wish).
This is because dispositions during terminal illness are treated like bequests, limited to one-third of the estate.
3
Note the effect of consent
If the daughters consent after the father's death (ijazah), the entire house becomes waqf upon them.
The consent of all heirs allows the full disposition to take effect, overriding the one-third limit.
4
Understand the legal reason
The one-third rule protects the interests of heirs; their consent shows they waive that protection, permitting the full waqf.
This is consistent with Hanafi rules on marad al-mawt dispositions.

Source Text

رجل وقف داراً له في مرضه على ثلاث بنات له وليس له وارث غيرهن قال الثلث من الدار وقف والثلثان مطلق له يصنعن بهما ما شئن . قال الفقيه أبو الليث هذا إذا لم يجزن، أما إذا أجزن صار الكل وقفاً عليهن اهـ.
A man made a waqf of his house in his illness upon his three daughters, and he has no heir other than them. He said: 'One-third of the house is waqf, and the two-thirds are absolutely theirs; they may do with them as they wish.' Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: 'This is if they do not consent. But if they consent, the whole becomes a waqf upon them.'
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling (mas'ala) stated by the author. A man in terminal illness makes a waqf of his house on his three daughters, who are his only heirs. Since the waqf is during marad al-mawt, it is limited to one-third of the estate. The remaining two-thirds are owned by the daughters as inheritance (each gets 2/9? Actually the two-thirds are divided among them equally as their fard and asabah? Since they are three daughters with no other heir, they inherit the whole estate, so the two-thirds is part of their inheritance. Abu al-Layth adds the qualification: if they do not consent to the waqf, the rule stands. But if they consent (after the father's death), then the entire house becomes waqf upon them, per their acceptance (ijazah). This illustrates the principle that the limitation to one-third is based on protecting the interests of other heirs; if there are no other heirs (or they all consent), the entire estate can be disposed of.

Key Terms
الإجازة (al-ijazah): Consent of the heirs after death to validate a disposition from the entire estate, not just one-third.

Key Takeaway
A disposition during terminal illness on one's only heirs is limited to one-third unless all heirs consent after death, which makes the entire disposition valid.

Judge's Ruling Cannot Make Waqf in Illness Binding
Refutation of invalid judicial decree

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that a judge's erroneous ruling cannot alter the substantive fiqh ruling on waqf in terminal illness.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling cannot make a non-binding act binding if it contradicts the revealed law.

This lesson examines a critical refinement by Ibn Nujaym regarding the limit of judicial authority. A common misconception holds that a judge's decree (qada) can retroactively confirm a waqf made during terminal illness as binding and irrevocable. Ibn Nujaym rejects this, affirming that the substantive fiqh ruling is independent of a judge's error. Understanding this reinforces the Hanafi principle that qada cannot change the underlying hukum—it only settles disputes within the bounds of Shariah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the erroneous ruling
The text mentions that some judges have ruled on the binding nature (luzum) of a waqf made in illness and declared the right of revocation (ruju') invalid. Recognize that this ruling contradicts the Hanafi view on waqf in marad al-mawt.
2
State the correct Hanafi position
Recall the Hanafi rule: According to Abu Hanifa, a waqf in terminal illness is not binding until death (the donor retains the right to revoke). According to the Sahibayn, it is binding only up to one-third. The judge's ruling that makes it fully binding and irrevocable contradicts these positions.
3
Analyze the error's source
The error lies in assuming that qada (judicial decree) can override or create a new fiqh ruling. In Hanafi usul, qada is limited to applying existing law; it cannot legislate or change a ruling based on clear proofs.
4
Apply the principle
Conclude that the judge's ruling is invalid ('laysa bi shay'), meaning it has no legal effect. The original fiqh ruling remains: the waqf is either non-binding (Abu Hanifa) or limited (Sahibayn). The heirs' rights are preserved despite the judge's error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القضاة قد قضى بلزوم هذا الوقف وبطلان حق الرجوع ليس بشيء في الصحيح؛ كذا في الكافي والخانية اهـ.
If the judges have ruled on the binding nature of this waqf and the invalidity of the right of revocation, it is nothing in the correct opinion; thus in al-Kafi and al-Khaniyya.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This brief statement from the author (Ibn Nujaym) is a critical refinement refuting an opinion that a judge's decree (qada) can make a waqf in illness binding and irreversible. The author declares that such a court ruling has no effect ('laysa bi shay') in the sahih (correct) position. This aligns with the Hanafi view that waqf in marad al-mawt is not binding until death (according to Abu Hanifa) or limited to one-third (Sahibayn). A judge's ruling cannot change the underlying fiqh. The sources cited (al-Kafi and al-Khaniyya) are standard Hanafi references.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada): Court judgment or decree by a judge.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness from which the person is expected to die; acts of donation during this period are subject to special rules to protect heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The ruling is invalid and has no effect in the correct view
D) The ruling is valid if the judge is a Hanafi

Key Takeaway
A judge's erroneous ruling cannot override the established fiqh ruling on waqf in terminal illness; such a ruling is null and void.

Corpus vs. Usufruct in Waqf During Illness
Critical correction of a waqf misstatement: corpus vs. usufruct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the corpus and usufruct of a waqf made during marad al-mawt and correct a common misinterpretation regarding the distribution of its revenue.

Core Idea
In waqf during illness, the corpus is limited to one-third; the usufruct is divided as inheritance among heirs during the beneficiary's lifetime.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critiques a problematic statement from al-Bazzaziyyah. Ibn Nujaym exposes a reading that would make the entire land inheritance, whereas the correct Hanafi position separates the owned two-thirds from the waqf one-third. Mastering this distinction is critical for correctly applying the rules of waqf in marad al-mawt and avoiding errors in property distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problematic statement
Extract the quoted statement from al-Bazzaziyyah: a waqf in illness on a son and descendants, with no heir consent, is called 'inheritance' among heirs while the son lives, then all goes to descendants. Note what seems wrong about it.
The statement appears to treat the entire land as inheritance, contradicting the one-third limitation.
2
Understand the corpus/usufruct distinction
Realise that the land's corpus (raqabah) is owned by heirs (two-thirds) and waqf (one-third). Only the usufruct (ghallah) of the one-third can be distributed differently. The statement must refer to the ghallah, not the land.
Ghalla = revenue like rent or produce.
3
Apply the one-third rule
In marad al-mawt, a waqf is limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent. Without consent, only one-third becomes waqf; the rest remains owned by heirs as inheritance.
4
Interpret the alternative response
Ibn Nujaym's teacher suggests the statement applies when the entire land equals one-third of the estate. In that case, the land wholly becomes waqf, but its ghallah is divided as inheritance until the beneficiary dies, then goes to descendants.
This reconciles the text with the principle.
5
Summarize the correct ruling
The waqf in illness is sahih but limited to one-third. The ghallah of that third is distributed among heirs according to inheritance shares while the beneficiary lives; after his death, it goes to subsequent beneficiaries.
This is the mufta bihi position per Ibn Nujaym.

So there is no conflict with what is in al-Zahiriyyah. Secondly, his statement 'then if he dies all of it goes to the descendants' contradicts it because the two-thirds are owned by the heir and the waqf is the one-third, so what becomes for the descendants is the revenue of this one-third, not the entire land. The apparent meaning is that this is the intention of the author. It is also possible to respond that the pronoun in his statement 'it is inheritance' refers to the revenue of the one-third that became waqf. And his statement 'then if he dies all of it goes to the descendants' means all the revenue of this one-third. As for the two-thirds, they are owned as corpus by the heirs. The indication of this intention is that what becomes for the heirs is that revenue of the one-third. So reflect. And our teacher responded with what is necessarily determined: his statement in al-Bazzaziyyah should be understood when the land comes out of one-third of the estate, then it all becomes waqf. Since they did not consent, its revenue is divided as inheritance, then after the son's death it all goes to the descendants, as clarified by the third case transmitted from al-Bazzaziyyah. Commentary
This extensive passage is a critical refinement by Ibn Nujaym (the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) of a statement he quotes from al-Bazzaziyyah. The statement says that a waqf in illness on a son and then descendants becomes inheritance among all heirs while the son lives, then after his death all goes to descendants. Ibn Nujaym initially calls this 'an incorrect expression' ('ibarah ghayr sahihah) and gives two reasons. First, it implies the land is owned by all heirs, but actually only two-thirds are owned; the one-third is waqf. He explains that the statement means the usufruct (ghallah) is distributed as inheritance, not the corpus. Second, the statement says after the son's death all goes to descendants, but that would contradict the heirs' ownership of the two-thirds. He resolves this by interpreting that only the usufruct of the one-third goes to descendants. Then he offers another response from his teacher (shaykh) that prefers to interpret the original statement as applying when the entire land is within the one-third of the estate (i.e., the estate is larger so the land equals one-third). In that case, the entire land becomes waqf, and if heirs do not consent, its usufruct is divided as inheritance until the son dies, then all usufruct goes to descendants. This interpretation is supported by another case in al-Bazzaziyyah. The passage also includes several other related rulings from al-Bazzaziyyah that support the correction.

Key Terms
الغلّة (al-ghallah): Revenue or usufruct generated by waqf property (e.g., rent or produce).
الرقبة (al-raqabah): The corpus or ownership of the property itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In waqf during marad al-mawt without heir consent, only the usufruct of the one-third portion is distributed as inheritance; the corpus of the two-thirds remains owned by the heirs.

8 min
Critique of a Waqf Statement in al-Bazaziyyah: Reconciling the One-Third Rule
Criticizing and reconciling a Bazaziyya ruling on waqf wording in marad al-mawt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the apparent contradiction in a waqf ruling from al-Bazaziyyah and apply the Hanafi principle of the one-third rule in marad al-mawt to resolve it.

Core Idea
A waqf in death illness is limited to one-third; any statement implying full ownership by heirs must be interpreted as referring to usufruct.

This lesson examines a specific waqf formulation from al-Bazaziyyah that appears to contradict the established Hanafi rule that only one-third of a sick person's estate can be subject to waqf. We will follow the critique by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and the reconciliation offered by his teacher, learning how apparent contradictions are resolved within the Hanafi tradition through careful analysis of wording and context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problematic statement
Read the Bazaziyya quote: declaring land as waqf on son then descendants, with heirs not permitting, results in the land being 'inheritance among the heirs' while the son lives, and 'all becomes for the descendants' after his death. Note that this seems to treat the entire land as inheritable or fully transferable to descendants.
The statement is from al-Bazaziyyah, a later Hanafi text.
2
Apply the one-third rule
Recall that in marad al-mawt, a waqf is treated like a bequest: it is limited to one-third of the estate without the heirs' consent. The remaining two-thirds remain property of the heirs and pass by inheritance.
This rule is derived from the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and is unanimous in the Hanafi school.
3
Recognize the contradiction
The Bazaziyya statement implies the land itself becomes inheritance among heirs, yet only one-third could be subject to waqf. If the whole land were inheritance, the waqf would be invalid. Also, saying it all becomes for descendants after the son's death contradicts the fact that only one-third is waqf.
The contradiction is between the literal wording and the established principle.
4
Analyze the author's critique
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq raises two objections: (1) if the land is inheritance, heirs would own the corpus, but they only own two-thirds; (2) after the son's death, only the produce of the one-third can go to descendants, not the entire land. He then provides answers: the first is resolved by interpreting 'inheritance' as referring to the produce distribution, not the corpus; the second by noting that the pronoun in 'it all becomes' refers to the produce of the third.
The author shows how to read the statement consistently with the one-third rule.
5
Apply the teacher's resolution
The teacher (shaykh) offers a definitive resolution: the Bazaziyya statement applies only when the land itself is within the one-third of the estate (i.e., its value does not exceed one-third of the total assets). In that case, the entire land becomes waqf from the outset, and its produce is distributed among the heirs like inheritance as long as the endowed son lives; after his death, the produce goes entirely to the descendants. This interpretation aligns with the third case cited from al-Bazaziyyah.
Thus, the apparent contradiction disappears when we assume the land is small enough to be fully covered by the one-third limit.

قال أرضي هذه صدقة موقوفة على ابني فلان فإن مات فعلى ولدي وولد ولدي ونسلي ولم تجز الورثة فهي إرث بين كل الورثة ما دام الابن الموقوف عليه حياً فإن مات صار كلها للنسل .اهـ. وهي عبارة غير صحيحة لما قدمنا وقف على ولد الولد بلا توقف على إجازة الورثة والثلثان للورثة إن لم يجيزوا، وإن أجازوا بين الصلبي وولد الولد على السواء. وقف أرضه في مرضه وهي تخرج من الثلث فتلف المال قبل موته وصار لا يخرج من الثلث أو تلف المال بعد موته قبل أن يصل إلى الورثة فثلثها وقف وثلثاها للورثة. وقف أرضه في مرضه على بعض ورثته فإن أجاز الورثة فهو كما قالوا في الوصية لبعض ورثته وإلا فإن كانت تخرج من الثلث صارت الأرض وقفاً، وإن لم تخرج فمقدار ما يخرج من الثلث يصير وقفاً ثم تقسم جميع غلة الأرض ما جاز فيه الوقف وما لم يجز على فرائض الله تعالى ما دام الموقوف عليه أو أحدهم في الأحياء، فإذا انقرضوا كلهم تصرف غلة الأرض إلى الفقراء حصة لهم من الوقف اهـ. ثم اعلم أنه لو وقفها في مرض موته ولا وارث له إلا زوجته ولم تجز ينبغي أن يكون كانت للوارث بلا منازع إلا إذا أجازها. هذا ما ظهر لي والله أعلم، قوله: (وهي عبارة غير صحيحة لوجهين: أحدهما أنه جعل الأرض إرثاً للورثة ومقتضاه أنها مملوكة لهم مع أن المملوك لهم ثلثاها فقط، وأيضاً إذا كانت مملوكة لهم كيف تصير بعد موت الابن للنسل ؟ والجواب أن قوله فهي إرث أي حكماً يعني أن غلتها تصرف بينهم على حكم الإرث وليس المراد أن نفس الأرض تكون إرثاً فليس بينهما وبين ما في الظهيرية مخالفة. ثانيهما قوله فإن مات صارت كلها للنسل» يخالفه فإن الثلثين ملك الوارث والموقوف هو الثلث فالذي تصير غلته للنسل هو هذا الثلث لا الأرض كلها، والظاهر أن هذا مراد المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى. ويمكن أن يجاب عنه بأن الضمير في قوله «فهي إرث» راجع إلى غلة الثلث الذي صار وقفاً. وقوله فإن مات صار كلها للنسل أي كل غلة هذا الثلث، وأما الثلثان فهما مملوكان رقبة للورثة والقرينة على هذه الإرادة أن الذي يصير للورثة هو تلك الغلة التي للثلث فتأمل. وأجاب شيخنا بما هو المتعين وهو أن يحمل كلام البزازية على ما إذا كانت الأرض تخرج من ثلث المال فإنها حينئذ تصير كلها وقفاً وحيث لم يجيزوا تقسم غلتها كالإرث ثم بعد موت الابن تصير كلها للنسل، ويوضحه المسألة الثالثة المنقولة عن البزازية أيضاً.
He said: This land of mine is a charity endowed upon my son so-and-so; then if he dies, upon my children and my children's children and my descendants, and the heirs did not permit it, then it is inheritance among all the heirs as long as the endowed-upon son is alive; then if he dies, it all becomes for the descendants. End quote. And it is an incorrect expression according to what we have previously mentioned from al-Zahiriyyah: that two-thirds are property and one-third is endowment, and that the produce of the third is distributed among the heirs as long as the endowed-upon heir is alive. And it is also indicated by what he mentioned in al-Bazaziyyah afterwards: He endowed his land in his illness upon his child and his child's child, and he had no property besides it, then one-third of it is an endowment upon the child's child without being contingent on the permission of the heirs, and two-thirds are for the heirs if they do not permit it; and if they permit, it is between the direct child and the child's child equally. He endowed his land in his illness while it was within the third, then the property perished before his death and it was no longer within the third, or the property perished after his death before reaching the heirs, then one-third of it is endowment and two-thirds are for the heirs. He endowed his land in his illness upon some of his heirs; if the heirs permit, it is as they said regarding a bequest to some of his heirs; otherwise, if it is within the third, the land becomes an endowment; if it is not within the third, then the amount that comes out of the third becomes an endowment, then all the produce of the land, both that which is permitted for endowment and that which is not, is divided according to the laws of Allah as long as the endowed-upon person or one of them is alive. Then when they all become extinct, the produce of the land is spent on the poor if the endower did not bequeath to any of the heirs. And if one of the endowed-upon from among the heirs dies and the others remain, then the deceased, in the division of the produce as long as the endowed-upon are alive, is treated as if he is alive and it is divided, then his share is made inheritance for his heirs who have no share in the endowment. End quote. Then know that if he endows it in his death illness and he has no heir except his wife and she does not permit, it should be that it is for the heir without dispute unless she permits it. This is what appeared to me, and Allah knows best. He said: (It is an incorrect expression for two reasons: First, he made the land inheritance for the heirs which implies that it is owned by them, while what is owned by them is only two-thirds of it. Also, if it is owned by them, how does it become for the descendants after the son's death? The answer: his saying 'it is inheritance' means legally, i.e., its produce is spent among them according to the rule of inheritance, not that the land itself is inheritance, so there is no contradiction between it and what is in al-Zahiriyyah. Second, his saying 'then if he dies, it all becomes for the descendants' contradicts that since two-thirds are owned by the heir and the endowed is one-third, so what becomes for the descendants is the produce of this one-third, not the entire land. It is apparent that this is the intention of the author, may Allah have mercy on him. It can be answered that the pronoun in his saying 'it is inheritance' refers to the produce of the third that became endowment, and his saying 'then if he dies, it all becomes for the descendants' means all the produce of this third. As for the two-thirds, they are owned in land (raqabah) by the heirs, and the evidence for this intention is that what becomes for the heirs is that produce of the third, so reflect. And our teacher answered with what is determined: that the statement of al-Bazaziyyah should be interpreted as referring to the case where the land is within the third of the property, for then it all becomes an endowment, and when they did not permit, its produce is divided like inheritance, then after the son's death it all becomes for the descendants. And it is clarified by the third issue transmitted from al-Bazaziyyah as well.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi commentary where the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critiques a statement from al-Bazaziyyah regarding a specific waqf wording made in marad al-mawt (death illness). The Bazaziyyah states: if someone says 'my land is a charity endowment on my son, then after his death on my children and descendants', and the heirs do not permit it, then the land is treated as inheritance among the heirs while the son is alive, and after his death it goes entirely to the descendants. The author finds this problematic because it contradicts the established principle from al-Zahiriyyah that only one-third of a sick person's estate can be subject to waqf (since it is treated as a bequest), and the remaining two-thirds remain property of the heirs. Therefore, the land cannot become entirely inheritance or entirely for the descendants. The author then provides three cases from al-Bazaziyyah itself as evidence that the correct ruling respects the one-third/two-thirds division. He then mentions his own opinion regarding a case where the only heir is a wife. Finally, he presents a detailed analysis with two objections and answers, concluding with his teacher's resolution: the Bazaziyyah's statement should be understood as applying only when the land is within the third of the estate (i.e., the total value of the land does not exceed one-third of the deceased's total assets), in which case it can indeed become entirely waqf. The teacher's answer explains that in that scenario, the land is all waqf from the outset, and the produce is divided among the heirs like inheritance as long as the endowed son lives; after his death, the produce goes entirely to the descendants. The author notes that this interpretation is supported by a third case in al-Bazaziyyah.

Key Terms
وقف (waqf): Endowment: a permanent dedication of property for charitable or family purposes, where the corpus is inalienable and only the usufruct is used.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Death illness: a sickness from which one does not expect to recover and which actually leads to death, making certain transactions subject to the one-third rule.
الثلث (al-thuluth): The third: the maximum portion of one's estate that can be disposed of via bequest or endowment in marad al-mawt without heirs' permission.
إرث (irth): Inheritance: the transfer of ownership of a deceased's property to heirs according to fixed shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's teacher in this passage, when does the Bazaziyyah's statement that the endowed land 'becomes entirely for the descendants' after the son's death apply?
A) When the heirs have all consented.
B) When the land is within the one-third of the estate.
C) When the endowment was made for the poor.
D) When the son had no children.

Key Takeaway
A waqf in death illness is limited to one-third; apparent contradictions in inherited texts are resolved by interpreting wording in light of established principles and contextual assumptions.

Ruling on Waqf in Marad al-Mawt with a Single Heir (Wife)
Ruling on waqf in marad al-mawt with sole heir wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a terminally ill person endows property leaving only a wife as heir, and explain the effect of her consent or lack thereof.

Core Idea
When a dying man endows all his property and only his wife survives, her lack of consent turns the endowment into inheritance for her.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in waqf law: a person in death illness (marad al-mawt) endows his entire property, but his only legal heir is his wife. Since the endowment exceeds the permissible one-third and the sole heir does not consent, what happens to the property? The author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a clear ruling based on the principle that the heir's lack of consent renders the excess invalid, so the wife takes the property as inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The case is a person in marad al-mawt who makes a waqf of his property, and his only heir is his wife. No other heirs exist.
Marad al-mawt is a death illness that triggers restrictions on gratuitous transfers beyond one-third.
2
Determine the condition
The key condition is whether the wife (the sole heir) permits the endowment. If she does not permit, the ruling changes.
If she permits, the waqf stands as declared. If she does not permit, the property goes to her as inheritance.
3
Apply the ruling without consent
Since she does not permit, the endowment beyond one-third is invalid, and the wife takes the entire property as her inheritance without any contest from others.
The author says 'it is for the heir without dispute' meaning no one else can claim it.
4
Note the consequence with consent
If she does permit, the waqf is effective and the property becomes a charitable endowment according to the declarant's terms.
This is the default rule for gifts in marad al-mawt: they require consent of heirs if exceeding one-third.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أنه لو وقفها في مرض موته ولا وارث له إلا زوجته ولم تجز ينبغي أن يكون كانت للوارث بلا منازع إلا إذا أجازها. هذا ما ظهر لي والله أعلم،
Then know that if he endows it in his death illness and he has no heir except his wife and she does not permit, it should be that it is for the heir without dispute unless she permits it. This is what appeared to me, and Allah knows best,
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the author regarding a specific scenario: a man in marad al-mawt endows his entire property, and his only heir is his wife. If the wife does not permit the endowment (since it exceeds the one-third limit), the endowment becomes valid for the heir (the wife) herself, meaning she takes the property as inheritance without any contest from others. If she does permit it, the endowment stands as declared. This is the author's own opinion (ظهر لي). The passage follows the earlier critique and is presented as an additional note.

Key Terms
وارث (warith): Heir: a person entitled to inherit from the deceased under Islamic inheritance law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a dying man endows his property and his only heir is his wife who does not permit it, what is the ruling according to the author?
A) The endowment is entirely invalid.
B) The property becomes charity for the poor.
C) The property is for the wife as inheritance without contest.
D) The wife must still honor the endowment.

Key Takeaway
When a terminally ill person endows property and only one heir survives, the heir's lack of consent renders the endowment invalid and the property returns as inheritance to that heir.

Bequest Calculation and Waqf Analogy with Wife as Sole Heir
Extracting a ruling on bequest analogized to waqf when wife is sole heir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the shares in a bequest when the sole heir is a wife and explain the Hanafi analogy between waqf in marad al-mawt and a bequest.

Core Idea
A waqf made during terminal illness is legally equivalent to a bequest: limited to one-third, but with a specific calculation when the wife is the sole heir.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a specific ruling from al-Bazaziyyah: a man on his deathbed bequeaths all his property to a stranger, leaving only his wife. The calculation of shares when she does not consent yields 1/6 for the wife and 5/6 for the legatee. The author then extends this ruling to waqf, affirming that waqf in terminal illness follows the same rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base case
The ruling from al-Bazaziyyah states that if a man dies leaving only his wife and bequeaths all his property to a non-heir, and the wife does not consent, she receives 1/6 and the legatee receives 5/6. This is the starting point for the analogy.
Take note of the arithmetic: the legatee first takes his one-third share, then the wife's share is taken from the remainder.
2
Trace the arithmetical derivation
Using a denominator of 12: total = 12. Legatee takes 4 (1/3). Remaining 8. Wife takes 2 (1/4 of 8 = 1/6 of total). Legatee then receives the remaining 6, giving him total 10/12 = 5/6. This calculation is the legal consequence when the only heir is a wife and the bequest is of the entire estate.
The wife's normal share (1/4) is reduced because the legatee's entitlement to one-third is prioritized.
3
Apply the analogy to waqf
The commentator asserts that waqf established during marad al-mawt (terminal illness) is legally identical to a bequest. Therefore, the same limitation (one-third of the estate without consent) and the same calculation apply when the only heir is a wife.
The illa (effective cause) is that both dispositions are made during death sickness, aiming to circumvent inheritance rules.
4
State the Hanafi ruling
Thus, if a terminally ill man makes a waqf of all his property to a non-heir, leaving only his wife, and she does not consent, the waqf is valid up to 5/6 of the estate (the legatee's share), and the wife takes 1/6 as her inheritance.
This ruling is specific to the scenario where the only heir is a wife; it does not apply to other combinations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي أوقاف الإمام يخرج من : لها السدس وخمسة الأسداس تكون وقفاً لما في البزازية من كتاب الوصايا : مات ولم يدع إلا امرأة واحدة وأوصى بكل ماله لرجل إن أجازت فكل المال له وإلا فالسدس لها وخمسة الأسداس له لأن الموصى له يأخذ الثلث أولاً بقي أربعة تأخذ الربع والثلاثة الباقية للموصى له فحصل له خمسة ستة اهـ. ولا شك أن الوقف في مرض الموت وصية.
And in Awqaf al-Imam it says: She gets one-sixth and five-sixths become an endowment, according to what is in al-Bazaziyyah from the Book of Wills: A man died leaving only one woman (wife) and bequeathed all his property to a man; if she consents, all the property is for him; otherwise, one-sixth is for her and five-sixths for him, because the legatee takes one-third first, then four remain, she takes one-quarter (of the remaining), and the remaining three are for the legatee, so he gets five-sixths. End quote. And there is no doubt that waqf in marad al-mawt is a bequest.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling from a work called 'Awqaf al-Imam' that is derived by analogy from a bequest case in al-Bazaziyyah's Book of Wills. The original case: a man dies leaving only his wife and makes a bequest of all his property to a non-heir (a stranger). The calculation is: first, the legatee is entitled to one-third of the estate (the maximum bequest without heirs' consent). Since the wife is the only heir, she gets her Quranic share (1/4 of the remaining? Actually the text says: after the legatee takes 1/3, 2/3 remains. The wife takes 1/4 of that 2/3? Let's calculate: Total property = 1. Legatee takes 1/3. Remaining 2/3. Wife’s share as wife is 1/4 of the estate (since no children) = 1/4 of 1 = 0.25. But the text says she takes a quarter of the four? Actually the text: 'أربعة تأخذ الربع' meaning 'four remain, she takes the quarter'. This suggests a denominator of 12: total 12 shares. Legatee takes 4 (1/3). Remaining 8. Wife takes 1/4 of remaining 8 = 2 shares. So legatee's total = 4 (from first) + remaining 6 (since wife took 2 of 8) = 10 shares = 10/12 = 5/6. Wife gets 2/12 = 1/6. So the legatee gets 5/6, wife 1/6. This is when she does not consent. If she consents, the legatee gets everything. The author then says there is no doubt that waqf in marad al-mawt is like a bequest (a will), thus the same calculation applies to waqf analogously.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): Bequest: a disposition of property to take effect after death, limited to one-third of the estate without heirs' consent.
وقف (waqf): Endowment: permanent dedication of property for charitable purposes, but in marad al-mawt it is treated as a bequest.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness: a disease from which death is expected, during which dispositions are treated as bequests.
سدس (sudus): One-sixth: the share the wife receives in this specific case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the bequest case from al-Bazaziyyah, if the wife does not consent, what share does the wife receive?
A) 1/3
B) 1/4
C) 1/6
D) 5/6

Key Takeaway
A waqf in terminal illness is functionally a bequest; when the only heir is a wife and she does not consent, she receives 1/6 and the non-heir beneficiary receives 5/6.

The First Type: Waqf for the Poor by a Sick Person
Ruling with rational proof (dalil aqli) based on analogy to bequests.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a sick person's waqf for the poor and apply the conditions of its validity (one-third rule and heirs' permission).

Core Idea
A sick person's waqf for the poor is valid in full only if within one-third; otherwise heirs' consent governs.

A person on their deathbed may still perform acts of charity, including waqf. Hanafi fiqh categorizes such waqfs based on the beneficiary and the estate limit. This lesson covers the first type: waqf upon the poor, detailing the role of the one-third rule and heirs' permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that this is a waqf made by a sick person (marad al-mawt) for the benefit of the poor. This is the first of four categories mentioned in al-Muhit.
The sick person's waqf is treated similarly to a bequest (wasiyya) in that it is limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs permit.
2
Understand the key condition: one-third of estate
The waqf is valid in its entirety if it does not exceed one-third of the estate. If it exceeds, the excess validity depends on heirs' consent.
The one-third rule is based on the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, limiting bequests to one-third.
3
Analyze the three scenarios
Scenario 1: The waqf is within one-third → valid wholly. Scenario 2: Exceeds one-third and heirs consent → valid wholly. Scenario 3: Exceeds and heirs do not consent → valid only to the extent of one-third (the rest is invalid).
4
Determine the practical ruling
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the waqf is valid according to these conditions. If invalid for the excess, that portion returns to the heirs as inheritance.
This ruling applies to all four types of waqf by a sick person.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : من وقف المريض على أربعة أوجه الأول أن يقف على الفقراء فإن خرج من الثلث جاز في الجميع وإلا فإن أجاز الورثة جاز في الكل وإلا جاز في الثلث الثاني لو وقف على وارث بعينه ولم يخرج من الثلث فإن لم يجيزوا جاز في الثلث. وذكر هلال غلة والخصاف تقسم جميع الأرض بين الورثة على فرائض الله تعالى ولا يعطى للفقراء شيء ما دام الموقوف عليه حياً، فإذا مات صرف للفقراء، فإن كان يخرج من الثلث يكون الكل للفقراء وإلا فلهم بقدر ما الثلث لأن هذا وقف على الفقراء بعد موت الوارث لا قبله فما دام الوارث حياً لا يكون وقفاً على الفقراء فلا يكون لهم حق في تلك الغلة والوصية للوارث قد بطلت فيقسم الكل بينهم بالسوية، وقال بعضهم : يعطى حصة الوقف من الغلة للفقراء للحال ولا يكون للورثة منها شيء لأن الوقف حصل على الفقراء للحال لأن هذا الوقف وصية بالغلة للوارث فإذا لم يجز الباقون بطلت الوصية للوارث فبقي هذا وقفاً على الفقراء، فأما إذا أجاز الورثة قيل تكون حصة الوقف للفقراء للحال، وقيل مقدار الثلث للفقراء وما وراء الثلث للموقوف عليه ما دام حياً، فإذا مات رجع إلى الورثة. والثالث لو وقف على المحتاجين من ولده ونسله ثم على الفقراء فإن كان الأولاد والنسل كلهم أغنياء فالغلة للفقراء، وإن كانوا كلهم فقراء أو كان في كل فريق بعضهم فقراء فإنه تقسم الغلة بينهم وبين فقراء الفريقين بالسوية، فما
And in al-Muhit: The waqf of a sick person is of four types: First: that he endows upon the poor. If it comes out of the third, it is valid in entirety; otherwise, if the heirs permit, it is valid in entirety; otherwise, it is valid in one-third. Second: if he endows upon a specific heir and it does not come out of the third; if they do not permit, it is valid in one-third. And Hilal mentioned: the produce – and al-Khassaf said: the entire land is divided among the heirs according to the laws of Allah, and nothing is given to the poor as long as the endowed-upon (heir) is alive. When he dies, it is spent on the poor. If it comes out of the third, everything goes to the poor; otherwise, they get to the extent of the third. Because this is an endowment on the poor after the heir's death, not before. So as long as the heir is alive, it is not an endowment on the poor, so they have no right to that produce, and the bequest to the heir has become void, so everything is divided among them equally. And some said: the share of the endowment from the produce is given to the poor immediately, and nothing goes to the heirs, because the endowment was made on the poor immediately; since this endowment is a bequest of the produce to the heir, if the remaining (heirs) do not permit, the bequest to the heir becomes void, so this remains an endowment on the poor. As for when the heirs permit, it is said: the share of the endowment is for the poor immediately; and it is said: the amount of one-third is for the poor, and what is beyond the third is for the endowed-upon as long as he lives, then when he dies, it returns to the heirs. Third: if he endows upon the needy among his children and descendants, then upon the poor; if the children and descendants are all rich, the produce is for the poor; if they are all poor or some in each group are poor, then the produce is divided between them and the poor of both groups equally. Then...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit categorizes the waqf of a sick person into four types, though only the first three are detailed here. The first type is a general endowment for the poor: if it does not exceed one-third of the estate, it is fully valid; if it exceeds, it depends on heirs' consent; otherwise valid only up to one-third. The second type is an endowment specifically for an heir: if it exceeds the third and heirs do not permit, only one-third is valid. There is a dispute regarding the distribution of produce during the heir's life: al-Khassaf says the land is divided among heirs as inheritance while the endowed-upon heir is alive, and nothing goes to the poor until his death; then the poor get what is within the third. Others argue the produce of the endowed share goes immediately to the poor. The third type is a layered endowment: first to needy descendants, then to the poor; the produce is distributed based on the financial status of the descendants. The passage provides the Hanafi position on these scenarios, citing al-Khassaf and other scholars.

Key Terms
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum amount a sick person can freely dispose of via bequest or waqf without heirs' consent.
المحيط (al-Muhit): A Hanafi legal work by Imam al-Sarakhsi, a key source for furu' al-fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A sick person endows $5,000 to the poor, and his total estate is $12,000. His heirs do not consent. How much of the waqf is valid?
A) $5,000
B) $4,000
C) $3,000
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
A sick person's waqf for the poor is valid only up to one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent to a larger amount.

The Second and Third Types: Waqf on an Heir and Layered Waqf
Ruling with rational proof and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings for a sick person's waqf on an heir and a layered waqf, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on distribution of produce.

Core Idea
A waqf on an heir during his life triggers a dispute: does the produce go to the poor immediately or only after his death?

The categories of a sick person's waqf become more intricate when the beneficiary is an heir or when multiple layers of beneficiaries are designated. This lesson explores the second and third types, focusing on the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the distribution of produce from a waqf on an heir.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the second type: waqf on a specific heir
The sick person endows property on a specific heir. If the endowment exceeds one-third and the other heirs do not permit, only one-third is valid.
The key issue is what happens to the produce (ghalla) of the endowed property during the heir's life.
2
Analyze the dispute on produce distribution
Al-Khassaf holds that the produce is divided among all heirs according to inheritance shares, and nothing goes to the poor during the heir's life. Another view says the produce of the endowed share goes to the poor immediately.
The difference hinges on whether the waqf is considered a bequest to the heir (void if not permitted) or a direct endowment to the poor from the start.
3
Understand the ruling for layered waqf (third type)
If the sick person endows on needy descendants first, then on the poor, the distribution depends on the financial status of the descendants: if all rich, produce goes to the poor; if all poor or mixed, produce is shared equally among the needy of both groups.
This type shows how a conditional or layered waqf works in Hanafi law.
4
Apply the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view in later Hanafi works is that of al-Khassaf: produce goes to heirs as inheritance until the heir dies, then to the poor within the one-third limit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : من وقف المريض على أربعة أوجه الأول أن يقف على الفقراء فإن خرج من الثلث جاز في الجميع وإلا فإن أجاز الورثة جاز في الكل وإلا جاز في الثلث الثاني لو وقف على وارث بعينه ولم يخرج من الثلث فإن لم يجيزوا جاز في الثلث. وذكر هلال غلة والخصاف تقسم جميع الأرض بين الورثة على فرائض الله تعالى ولا يعطى للفقراء شيء ما دام الموقوف عليه حياً، فإذا مات صرف للفقراء، فإن كان يخرج من الثلث يكون الكل للفقراء وإلا فلهم بقدر ما الثلث لأن هذا وقف على الفقراء بعد موت الوارث لا قبله فما دام الوارث حياً لا يكون وقفاً على الفقراء فلا يكون لهم حق في تلك الغلة والوصية للوارث قد بطلت فيقسم الكل بينهم بالسوية، وقال بعضهم : يعطى حصة الوقف من الغلة للفقراء للحال ولا يكون للورثة منها شيء لأن الوقف حصل على الفقراء للحال لأن هذا الوقف وصية بالغلة للوارث فإذا لم يجز الباقون بطلت الوصية للوارث فبقي هذا وقفاً على الفقراء، فأما إذا أجاز الورثة قيل تكون حصة الوقف للفقراء للحال، وقيل مقدار الثلث للفقراء وما وراء الثلث للموقوف عليه ما دام حياً، فإذا مات رجع إلى الورثة. والثالث لو وقف على المحتاجين من ولده ونسله ثم على الفقراء فإن كان الأولاد والنسل كلهم أغنياء فالغلة للفقراء، وإن كانوا كلهم فقراء أو كان في كل فريق بعضهم فقراء فإنه تقسم الغلة بينهم وبين فقراء الفريقين بالسوية، فما
And in al-Muhit: The waqf of a sick person is of four types: First: that he endows upon the poor. If it comes out of the third, it is valid in entirety; otherwise, if the heirs permit, it is valid in entirety; otherwise, it is valid in one-third. Second: if he endows upon a specific heir and it does not come out of the third; if they do not permit, it is valid in one-third. And Hilal mentioned: the produce – and al-Khassaf said: the entire land is divided among the heirs according to the laws of Allah, and nothing is given to the poor as long as the endowed-upon (heir) is alive. When he dies, it is spent on the poor. If it comes out of the third, everything goes to the poor; otherwise, they get to the extent of the third. Because this is an endowment on the poor after the heir's death, not before. So as long as the heir is alive, it is not an endowment on the poor, so they have no right to that produce, and the bequest to the heir has become void, so everything is divided among them equally. And some said: the share of the endowment from the produce is given to the poor immediately, and nothing goes to the heirs, because the endowment was made on the poor immediately; since this endowment is a bequest of the produce to the heir, if the remaining (heirs) do not permit, the bequest to the heir becomes void, so this remains an endowment on the poor. As for when the heirs permit, it is said: the share of the endowment is for the poor immediately; and it is said: the amount of one-third is for the poor, and what is beyond the third is for the endowed-upon as long as he lives, then when he dies, it returns to the heirs. Third: if he endows upon the needy among his children and descendants, then upon the poor; if the children and descendants are all rich, the produce is for the poor; if they are all poor or some in each group are poor, then the produce is divided between them and the poor of both groups equally. Then...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit categorizes the waqf of a sick person into four types, though only the first three are detailed here. The first type is a general endowment for the poor: if it does not exceed one-third of the estate, it is fully valid; if it exceeds, it depends on heirs' consent; otherwise valid only up to one-third. The second type is an endowment specifically for an heir: if it exceeds the third and heirs do not permit, only one-third is valid. There is a dispute regarding the distribution of produce during the heir's life: al-Khassaf says the land is divided among heirs as inheritance while the endowed-upon heir is alive, and nothing goes to the poor until his death; then the poor get what is within the third. Others argue the produce of the endowed share goes immediately to the poor. The third type is a layered endowment: first to needy descendants, then to the poor; the produce is distributed based on the financial status of the descendants. The passage provides the Hanafi position on these scenarios, citing al-Khassaf and other scholars.

Key Terms
الغلة (al-ghalla): The produce or revenue generated from the endowed property, such as rent, crop yield, or profit.
الوصية (al-wasiyya): Bequest; the designation of a benefit to someone after death, subject to the one-third rule.
الخصاف (al-Khassaf): A prominent Hanafi jurist known for his works on waqf and inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khassaf, what happens to the produce of a waqf on an heir while that heir is alive?
A) It is given to the poor.
B) It is given to the heir.
C) It is divided among all heirs according to inheritance shares.
D) It is held in trust for the poor until the heir dies.

Key Takeaway
In a sick person's waqf on an heir, the produce is distributed as inheritance during the heir's life according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, and only after the heir's death does it go to the poor.

Waqf — Endowment
