12 min
Al-Khassaf's Waqf for Lineage: Heirs and Non-Heirs in Marad al-Mawt
Detailed case from al-Khassaf on waqf for lineage then poor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for a waqf made in marad al-mawt where beneficiaries include both heirs and non-heirs, and distinguish the distribution of produce when the waqf is within or exceeds the one-third limit.

Core Idea
A bequest to an heir is invalid; thus a waqf benefiting heirs and non-heirs forces redistribution of the heir's share among all heirs.

Al-Khassaf presents a classic scenario: a sick man endows land for his descendants (children and grandchildren) then for the poor. Because this is a bequest-like transaction in marad al-mawt, the one-third limitation applies. Moreover, since the beneficiaries include both heirs (direct children) and non-heirs (grandchildren who may not inherit), the distribution of the produce must respect the prohibition of bequest to an heir. This lesson walks through the two scenarios—within the third and exceeding it—and clarifies how the produce is allocated and redistributed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key elements of the waqf
Note that the waqf is made by a sick person (marad al-mawt), for his lineage (direct children, grandchildren, descendants) perpetually, then for the poor. The property is land. The issue: treat as bequest, so one-third rule applies.
In Hanafi fiqh, a waqf in marad al-mawt is governed by the law of bequests, not inter vivos gifts.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios: within one-third vs. exceeding one-third
If the land is within one-third of the estate, the entire waqf is valid. If it exceeds one-third, only one-third becomes waqf; the remainder is inheritance to the heirs as per normal rules.
3
For within one-third: trace the distribution of produce
The produce is first divided among all heirs (including direct children and grandchildren if they are heirs) according to inheritance shares. But the portion that goes to direct children (heirs) must be redistributed among all heirs because a bequest to an heir is invalid without consent. The portion going to non-heir grandchildren stays with them.
The redistribution treats the direct child's share as inheritance, not as a bequest benefit.
4
For exceeding one-third: trace the partial waqf distribution
Only one-third of the land is waqf. Its produce is divided between direct children and grandchildren (if both exist). But again, the direct child's share (being an heir) is redistributed among all other heirs. The rest (two-thirds of land) is inherited normally.
After the direct children die out, the entire waqf produce goes to the poor as specified.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The key rule: when a waqf (or bequest) in marad al-mawt benefits an heir, that benefit is invalid unless all heirs consent. Here, the waqf is for the lineage; the direct children are heirs, so their share of produce must be treated as inheritance and distributed among all heirs. Grandchildren may be non-heirs (if their parents are alive), so they receive their share directly.
This demonstrates the intersection of waqf, inheritance, and bequest law in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فما الخصاف: لو أن رجلاً مريضاً قال أرضي هذه صدقة موقوفة الله أبداً على ولده وولد ولده ونسله وعقبه أبداً ما تناسلوا ثم من بعدهم على المساكين، فإن كانت هذه الأرض تخرج من الثلث أخرجت وكانت موقوفة تستغل ثم تقسم غلتها على جميع ورثته على قدر مواريثهم عنه، فإن كان له ولد لصلبه وله ولد ولد قسمت الغلة على عدد ولده لصلبه وعلى عدد ولد ولده فما أصاب من ذلك ولده قسم من بين ورثته جميعاً على عدد مواريثهم من قبل أن هذه وصية والوصية للوارث لا تجوز، فما أصاب من ذلك من يرثه من ولده من غلة هذا الوقف قسم ذلك بين جميع ورثة الواقف على قدر مواريثهم عنه ، وما أصاب من لا يرثه من ولد ولده من هذه الغلة كان ذلك لهم، فإذا انقرض ولده لصلبه قسمت غلة هذه الصدقة بين ولد ولده ونسله على ما قال ولا يكون لزوجته ولا لأبويه من ذلك شيء، فإن انا كانت هذه الأرض لا تخرج من ثلث مال الواقف قال : يكون ثلثاها ميران بين جميع ورثته على قدر مواريثهم عنه ويكون ثلثها موقوفاً تقسم غلته إذا جاءت على ولده لصلبه وولد ولده جميعاً إن كان له ولد وولد ولد، فما أصاب ولده لصلبه يقسم ذلك بين سائر ورثته على قدر مواريثهم، فإذا انقرضوا أنفذت الغلة على ما سبلها الواقف اهـ .
Then al-Khassaf: If a sick man said, 'This land of mine is a charity endowed perpetually for Allah for my child, my child's child, my descendants and progeny forever as long as they multiply, then after them for the poor.' If this land comes out of the third of his estate, it is taken out and becomes an endowment; its produce is collected and then divided among all his heirs according to their inheritance shares. So if he has a direct child and a child's child, the produce is divided according to the number of his direct children and the number of his child's children. What befalls his direct children from that is divided among all his heirs according to their inheritance shares because this is a bequest, and a bequest to an heir is not valid. What befalls those of his children who do not inherit from the produce of this endowment is divided among all the heirs of the waqif according to their inheritance shares. And what befalls those of his child's children who do not inherit from this produce is for them. Then when his direct children become extinct, the produce of this charity is divided among his child's children and descendants as he said, and his wife and parents get nothing from it. If this land does not come out of the third of the waqif's property, he said: two-thirds of it are inheritance among all his heirs according to their inheritance shares, and one-third is an endowment; its produce, when it comes, is divided among his direct child and child's child together if he has a child and a child's child. What befalls his direct child from that is divided among all his other heirs according to their inheritance shares. When they become extinct, the produce is executed as the waqif specified. End quote.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage from al-Khassaf presents a comprehensive case of a waqf made by a sick man for his lineage (children, grandchildren, etc.) and then for the poor. The ruling has two scenarios: (1) If the land is within the one-third of the estate, it becomes waqf immediately. Its produce is divided among the heirs (not the beneficiaries) as inheritance, because a bequest to an heir is invalid; but here the waqf is for all descendants, some of whom may be heirs and some non-heirs. The portion that goes to the direct children (who are heirs) must be redistributed among all heirs, while the portion for the child's children (if they are non-heirs) stays with them. After the direct children die out, the whole produce goes to the remaining descendants as specified. (2) If the land exceeds one-third, only one-third becomes waqf, and the rest (two-thirds) is inheritance. The produce of the waqf portion is divided between direct children and grandchildren; but the share of direct children (heirs) is again redistributed among all other heirs. Eventually, after the direct children die, the produce goes as per the waqf specification (to the poor). This case illustrates the complexity of waqf in marad al-mawt when beneficiaries include both heirs and non-heirs, and the one-third limitation applies.

Key Terms
الخصاف (al-Khassaf): A Hanafi jurist and author of works on waqf and other topics; his opinions are often cited in later Hanafi texts.
الوصية للوارث لا تجوز (al-wasiyyah li al-warith la tujuz): A bequest to an heir is not valid (without the consent of other heirs).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In al-Khassaf's case, when the land is within the third, what happens to the portion of produce that goes to the direct child of the waqif?
A) It is given entirely to the child.
B) It is divided among all heirs according to inheritance shares.
C) It is given to the poor immediately.
D) It is held for the child until death.

Key Takeaway
When a waqf in marad al-mawt includes both heirs and non-heirs, the produce must be distributed according to inheritance shares, with the heir's share redistributed among all heirs due to the prohibition of bequest to an heir.

Types One and Two of Waqf in Terminal Illness
Categorizes waqf in terminal illness into four types, focusing on the first two

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the first two types of waqf in marad al-mawt and apply the one-third rule to each.

Core Idea
A waqf in terminal illness is treated as a will — limited to one-third unless heirs permit.

This lesson examines the first two categories of waqf during terminal illness as outlined in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author establishes the foundational principle that such a waqf is akin to a testamentary disposition (wasiyya). We will learn how the one-third rule applies when the waqf is for charity or for a specific heir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing principle
The author states that waqf in marad al-mawt is treated as a will. Why is this classification important? It brings the one-third limit and heir consent rules into effect.
2
Analyze the first type: waqf for the poor
If the waqf is within one-third, it is fully valid. If it exceeds, it is valid only in one-third unless the heirs permit the whole.
Heirs' consent can validate the entire waqf even if it exceeds one-third.
3
Analyze the second type: waqf for a specific heir
A waqf for an heir is invalid in excess of one-third without heir consent. If the heirs do not permit, only one-third is valid as a bequest.
This prevents donors from disinheriting other heirs through bequests to specific heirs.
4
Apply to the opening case
In the example from al-Bazzaziyya, a man dies leaving only a wife and bequeaths all to a stranger. The wife's inheritance is one-sixth; the legatee gets the rest. This illustrates the interplay between inheritance and bequest.
The wife's permission is not required for the bequest because the stranger is a non-heir; her share is protected.

She gets one-sixth and five-sixths become waqf, as in al-Bazzaziyya from the chapter of wills: A man died leaving only one wife and bequeathed all his property to a man. If she permits, all is for him; otherwise, one-sixth is for her and five-sixths for him because the legatee takes one-third first, then four remain, she takes one-fourth, and the remaining three are for the legatee, so he gets five-sixths. There is no doubt that waqf in terminal illness is a will. In al-Muhit: The waqf of a sick person is of four types: First, that he makes waqf for the poor. If it is within one-third, it is valid in all; otherwise, if the heirs permit, it is valid in all; otherwise, it is valid in one-third. Second, if he makes waqf for a specific heir and it is not within one-third, and they do not permit, it is valid in one-third. Hilal mentioned produce, and al-Khassaf: All the land is divided among the heirs according to Allah's inheritance shares, and nothing is given to the poor as long as the beneficiary is alive; when he dies, it is given to the poor. If it is within one-third, all is for the poor; otherwise, they get according to one-third because this is waqf for the poor after the heir's death, not before. As long as the heir is alive, it is not waqf for the poor, so they have no right to that produce, and the bequest to the heir is invalidated, so the whole is divided equally among them. Some said: The share of waqf from the produce is given to the poor immediately, and the heirs have nothing because the waqf was for the poor immediately, since this waqf is a bequest of produce to the heir; if the others do not permit, the bequest to the heir is invalidated, and this remains waqf for the poor. As for when the heirs permit, it is said the waqf share is for the poor immediately; it is also said the amount of one-third is for the poor and what is beyond one-third is for the beneficiary as long as he lives, then when he dies it returns to the heirs. Third, if he makes waqf for the needy among his children and descendants, then for the poor: if all children and descendants are rich, the produce is for the poor; if they are all poor or in each group some are poor, the produce is divided equally between them and the poor of the two groups. Al-Khassaf: If a sick man says, 'This land of mine is charity, waqf for Allah forever for my children, grandchildren, descendants, and posterity forever as long as they continue, then after them for the needy,' then if this land is within one-third, it is taken out and made waqf, its produce is divided among all his heirs according to their shares of inheritance. If he has a direct child and a grandchild, the produce is divided according to the number of direct children and grandchildren. What falls to his direct child is divided among all his heirs according to their shares of inheritance because this is a will, and a will for an heir is not valid. What falls to a grandchild who is not an heir from this produce is theirs. When the direct children are extinct, the produce of this charity is divided among grandchildren and descendants as stated, and his wife and parents get nothing from it. If this land is not within one-third of the testator's wealth, two-thirds are inheritance among all his heirs according to their shares, and one-third is waqf; its produce when it comes is divided among his direct children and grandchildren, if he has a child and grandchild. What falls to his direct child is divided among his other heirs according to their shares; when they are extinct, the produce is used as the waqf founder directed. The waqf of the property is validated, and whatever falls to the poor from the direct children is divided between the rich and poor according to Allah's inheritance shares. What falls to the poor from the descendants is divided equally among them, excluding the rich among them. If the direct children are all rich and the descendants are poor, all produce is for the descendants equally. If the opposite, or some direct children are poor, all produce is for the direct children divided according to Allah's inheritance shares, because what falls to descendants is by way of bequest since they are not heirs, so it is among them equally; what falls to children is by inheritance since there is no bequest for an heir, so it is among them according to their inheritance shares. Fourth, if he bequeaths that his land be made waqf after his death for poor Muslims: if it is within one-third or the heirs permit, it is all made waqf; if they do not permit, one-third is made waqf, considering the part as the whole. If it is all within one-third and it has date palms that bear fruit after death but before the land is made waqf, the fruit enters the waqf because it came from an asset occupied by the right of those entitled to the waqf. If it bore fruit before death, that fruit is inheritance. The completion is in al-Is'af with explanation of the ruling on a sick person's acknowledgment of waqf.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rulings of waqf made during terminal illness (marad al-mawt), which is treated as a testamentary disposition (wasiyya). The author opens by citing a case from al-Bazzaziyya where a man leaves only a wife and bequeaths all property to a stranger; if the wife permits, all goes to the legatee; if not, she takes her Qur'anic share (1/6) and the legatee gets the remainder (5/6). The key principle is that waqf in illness is like a will: it is subject to the one-third rule and requires heir consent if it exceeds one-third or is for an heir. The author then presents four types from al-Muhit: (1) waqf for the poor – valid entirely if within one-third, otherwise only one-third unless heirs permit; (2) waqf for a specific heir – valid only in one-third without heir consent; (3) waqf for needy children and descendants then the poor – complex distribution rules based on whether beneficiaries are heirs and their poverty status, with detailed calculations from al-Khassaf; (4) bequest to have land turned into waqf after death – same one-third rule, with additional ruling that fruit produced after death but before the waqf is executed enters the waqf. The passage concludes by noting the full discussion is in al-Is'af. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each type and sub-case, focusing on the interplay between the one-third limit, heir consent, and the distinction between inheritance and bequest for heirs.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A terminal illness that makes a person's dispositions subject to will rules (one-third, no bequest to heir without consent).
الوصية (al-wasiyya): A bequest; a disposition of property taking effect after death, limited to one-third of the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a terminally ill person makes a waqf for a specific heir that exceeds one-third, and the other heirs do not permit, what portion is valid?
A) The entire waqf, because it is charitable
B) None, because bequests to heirs are invalid
C) One-third of the waqf
D) Only the amount that the heir would inherit anyway

Key Takeaway
Waqf made during terminal illness is treated as a will, so it is limited to one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent to more.

Waqf — Endowment

Type Three and Four: Waqf for Descendants and Bequest to Create Waqf
Details the third and fourth types of waqf in marad al-mawt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate distributions for a waqf on children and descendants then the poor, and apply the ruling for a bequest to create a waqf after death.

Core Idea
Waqf for descendants then the poor requires splitting proceeds between heirs and non-heirs according to inheritance and bequest rules.

This lesson delves into the third and fourth types of waqf in terminal illness from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The third type involves a waqf for needy children and descendants, then the poor, with complex distribution depending on the financial status of beneficiaries. The fourth type is a bequest to have land turned into waqf after death, with an additional ruling on fruit produced after death.

Guided Path
1
Understand the structure of Type Three
The waqf is first for the needy among the donor's children and descendants, then for the poor after their extinction. The distribution of produce depends on whether the children and descendants are rich or poor, and whether they are heirs.
2
Analyze the base case from al-Khassaf
If the land is within one-third, it is made waqf and its produce is divided among all heirs by inheritance shares. The portion falling to direct children (who are heirs) is then redistributed among all heirs again because a bequest to an heir is invalid. Descendants who are not heirs keep their portion.
This double distribution ensures that the children's share does not become a bequest to them.
3
Apply the rule when the waqf exceeds one-third
Two-thirds remain inheritance; one-third is waqf. The produce of the one-third is divided among children and grandchildren. The children's portion is again redistributed among all heirs.
The one-third portion is treated exactly like a will.
4
Analyze Type Four: bequest to create a waqf
If a person bequeaths that his land be made waqf for the poor after his death, the one-third rule applies. Additionally, fruit produced after death but before the waqf is executed enters the waqf.
Fruit produced before death is inheritance.

She gets one-sixth and five-sixths become waqf, as in al-Bazzaziyya from the chapter of wills: A man died leaving only one wife and bequeathed all his property to a man. If she permits, all is for him; otherwise, one-sixth is for her and five-sixths for him because the legatee takes one-third first, then four remain, she takes one-fourth, and the remaining three are for the legatee, so he gets five-sixths. There is no doubt that waqf in terminal illness is a will. In al-Muhit: The waqf of a sick person is of four types: First, that he makes waqf for the poor. If it is within one-third, it is valid in all; otherwise, if the heirs permit, it is valid in all; otherwise, it is valid in one-third. Second, if he makes waqf for a specific heir and it is not within one-third, and they do not permit, it is valid in one-third. Hilal mentioned produce, and al-Khassaf: All the land is divided among the heirs according to Allah's inheritance shares, and nothing is given to the poor as long as the beneficiary is alive; when he dies, it is given to the poor. If it is within one-third, all is for the poor; otherwise, they get according to one-third because this is waqf for the poor after the heir's death, not before. As long as the heir is alive, it is not waqf for the poor, so they have no right to that produce, and the bequest to the heir is invalidated, so the whole is divided equally among them. Some said: The share of waqf from the produce is given to the poor immediately, and the heirs have nothing because the waqf was for the poor immediately, since this waqf is a bequest of produce to the heir; if the others do not permit, the bequest to the heir is invalidated, and this remains waqf for the poor. As for when the heirs permit, it is said the waqf share is for the poor immediately; it is also said the amount of one-third is for the poor and what is beyond one-third is for the beneficiary as long as he lives, then when he dies it returns to the heirs. Third, if he makes waqf for the needy among his children and descendants, then for the poor: if all children and descendants are rich, the produce is for the poor; if they are all poor or in each group some are poor, the produce is divided equally between them and the poor of the two groups. Al-Khassaf: If a sick man says, 'This land of mine is charity, waqf for Allah forever for my children, grandchildren, descendants, and posterity forever as long as they continue, then after them for the needy,' then if this land is within one-third, it is taken out and made waqf, its produce is divided among all his heirs according to their shares of inheritance. If he has a direct child and a grandchild, the produce is divided according to the number of direct children and grandchildren. What falls to his direct child is divided among all his heirs according to their shares of inheritance because this is a will, and a will for an heir is not valid. What falls to a grandchild who is not an heir from this produce is theirs. When the direct children are extinct, the produce of this charity is divided among grandchildren and descendants as stated, and his wife and parents get nothing from it. If this land is not within one-third of the testator's wealth, two-thirds are inheritance among all his heirs according to their shares, and one-third is waqf; its produce when it comes is divided among his direct children and grandchildren, if he has a child and grandchild. What falls to his direct child is divided among his other heirs according to their shares; when they are extinct, the produce is used as the waqf founder directed. The waqf of the property is validated, and whatever falls to the poor from the direct children is divided between the rich and poor according to Allah's inheritance shares. What falls to the poor from the descendants is divided equally among them, excluding the rich among them. If the direct children are all rich and the descendants are poor, all produce is for the descendants equally. If the opposite, or some direct children are poor, all produce is for the direct children divided according to Allah's inheritance shares, because what falls to descendants is by way of bequest since they are not heirs, so it is among them equally; what falls to children is by inheritance since there is no bequest for an heir, so it is among them according to their inheritance shares. Fourth, if he bequeaths that his land be made waqf after his death for poor Muslims: if it is within one-third or the heirs permit, it is all made waqf; if they do not permit, one-third is made waqf, considering the part as the whole. If it is all within one-third and it has date palms that bear fruit after death but before the land is made waqf, the fruit enters the waqf because it came from an asset occupied by the right of those entitled to the waqf. If it bore fruit before death, that fruit is inheritance. The completion is in al-Is'af with explanation of the ruling on a sick person's acknowledgment of waqf.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rulings of waqf made during terminal illness (marad al-mawt), which is treated as a testamentary disposition (wasiyya). The author opens by citing a case from al-Bazzaziyya where a man leaves only a wife and bequeaths all property to a stranger; if the wife permits, all goes to the legatee; if not, she takes her Qur'anic share (1/6) and the legatee gets the remainder (5/6). Key Terms
النسل (al-nasl): Descendants; offspring including children and grandchildren.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third; the maximum portion for testamentary dispositions.

Delivery and Segregation in Waqf: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on waqf delivery conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on the necessity of delivery for waqf completion and explain the practical consequence of each.

Core Idea
For waqf to be binding, Abu Yusuf says mere declaration suffices; Muhammad requires actual delivery.

The matn states that waqf is not completed until it is received, segregated, and made perpetual. This reflects the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani. But Abu Yusuf holds a different position: waqf is binding by mere declaration, just like manumission. This lesson unpacks the arguments and explores how later Hanafi jurists differed on which view to follow in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's ruling
The matn says: 'It is not completed until it is received, segregated, and its end is made for an unceasing direction.' This is the view of Muhammad. Note that the matn author followed Muhammad in conditions but earlier followed Abu Hanifa on other aspects.
The matn itself is not neutral; it adopts Muhammad's view.
2
Contrast the two Hanafi positions
Abu Yusuf: waqf is binding by mere declaration, analogy to manumission (itq). Muhammad: waqf requires delivery to the trustee (qabd), segregation (ifraz), and perpetuity (ta'bid). Understand their dalil: Abu Yusuf says ownership is eliminated by declaration; Muhammad says waqf is like charity, where delivery is needed because the dedication to Allah is not a direct transfer.
Both are Hanafi; the ikhtilaf is within the school.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Yusuf's qiyas: waqf eliminates ownership just as itq does. Muhammad's view: waqf establishes a right of Allah, which is realized through delivery to the trustee, similar to zakat and sadaqah. The text gives an example: saying 'this tree is for the mosque' does not make it waqf without handing it over.
The example shows a clear practical difference.
4
Survey the later fatwa positions
The text lists multiple authorities: Balkh scholars favor Abu Yusuf; al-Sadr al-Shahid, most regions, and Bukharans favor Muhammad; Fath al-Qadir says Abu Yusuf is more appropriate for researchers; al-Munya gives fatwa on Abu Yusuf. There is no single tarjih.
The multiplicity of fatwa positions shows the enduring disagreement.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If a person says 'I make waqf of my house' but does not deliver it, under Abu Yusuf it is binding; under Muhammad it is not valid until delivery. This affects estate planning and the validity of quick declarations.
Always check which view is operative in your locale or case.

قوله: (ولا يتم حتى يقبض ويفرز ويجعل آخره لجهة لا تنقطع بيان لشرائطه الخاصة على قول محمد وقد مشى المؤلف أولاً على قول أبي حنيفة من عدم لزومه إلا بالقضاء وثانياً في الشرائط على قول لأن الفتوى على قولهما في لزومه بلا قضاء كما قدمنا، وإذا لزم عندهما فإنه يلزم بمجرد القول عند أبي يوسف بمنزلة الإعتاق بجامع إسقاط الملك، محمد لا بد من التسليم إلى المتولي والإفراز والتأبيد. أما الأول فلأن حق الله تعالى إنما يثبت محمد وهو مما لا ينبغي وعند فيه في ضمن التسليم إلى العبد لأن التمليك إلى الله تعالى وهو مالك الأشياء لا يتحقق مقصوداً وقد يكون تبعاً لغيره فيأخذه حكمه فينزل منزلة الزكاة والصدقة. فلو قال هذه الشجرة للمسجد لا تكون له ما لم يسلمها إلى قيم المسجد عند محمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف. وفي الخلاصة : ومشايخ بلخ يفتون بقول أبي يوسف وقال الصدر الشهيد: والفتوى على قول محمد. وفي شرح المجمع أكثر فقهاء الأمصار أخذوا بقول محمد والفتوى عليه. وفي فتح القدير : وقول أبي يوسف أوجه عند المحققين. وفي المنية الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف. وهذا قول مشايخ بلخ، وأما البخاريون فأخذوا بقول محمد وفي المبسوط : كان القاضي أبو عاصم يقول: قول أبي يوسف من حيث المعنى أقوى إلا أنه قال: وقول محمد أقرب إلى موافقة الآثار يعني ما روي أن عمر رضي الله عنه جعل وقفه في يد حفصة وغير ذلك. ورده في المبسوط بأنه لا يلزم كونه ليتم الوقف بل لشغله وخوف التقصير إلى آخره. وفي البزازية : والإمام الثاني في قوله الأول ضيق ثم وسع كل التوسع حتى قال يتم بقوله وقفت ومشايخ قوله : (وقد مشى المؤلف أولا على قول أبي حنيفة قال في النهر : الأولى أن يحمل ما قاله أولاً
His statement: '(It is not completed until it is received, segregated, and its end is made for an unceasing direction)' is an explanation of its special conditions according to the view of Muhammad. The author first followed the view of Abu Hanifa that it is not binding except by judicial decree, and second in the conditions he followed the view because the fatwa is on the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding its binding without judicial decree as we presented. When it becomes binding according to them, then it is binding by mere statement according to Abu Yusuf, analogous to manumission due to the common factor of eliminating ownership. According to Muhammad, delivery to the administrator, segregation, and perpetuity are necessary. As for the first, because the right of Allah is established within delivery to the servant, since making ownership for Allah (who is the owner of all things) is not realized intentionally and may be secondary to others, so it takes its ruling and is treated like zakat and charity. For instance, if one says 'This tree is for the mosque,' it does not become for it unless he delivers it to the mosque's caretaker according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. In al-Khulasa: The scholars of Balkh give fatwa according to Abu Yusuf, while al-Sadr al-Shahid said the fatwa is on Muhammad's view. In Sharh al-Majma': Most jurists of the regions adopted Muhammad's view and the fatwa is upon it. In Fath al-Qadir: Abu Yusuf's view is more appropriate according to the researchers. In al-Munya: The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view, and this is the view of the scholars of Balkh. As for the Bukharans, they adopted Muhammad's view. In al-Mabsut: Judge Abu Asim used to say: Abu Yusuf's view is stronger in terms of meaning, except he said: Muhammad's view is closer to conformity with reports, meaning what is narrated that Umar placed his waqf in the hand of Hafsa and other than that. Al-Mabsut refuted this by saying that this does not necessitate that it completes the waqf, but rather for management and fear of negligence etc. In al-Bazzaziyya: The second Imam (Abu Yusuf) in his first view was strict, then he expanded greatly until he said it is completed by his saying 'I have made waqf'. And the scholars... His statement: (And the author first followed the view of Abu Hanifa). In al-Nahr: It is better to interpret what he said first...
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the conditions for the validity and completion of waqf. The author comments on the matn 'It is not completed until it is received, segregated, and its end is made for an unceasing direction.' This is identified as the special conditions according to Muhammad al-Shaybani. The author notes that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq first followed Abu Hanifa's view that waqf is not binding without judicial decree, but in the conditions he followed the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because fatwa is on their view that waqf is binding without decree. The key ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf holds that waqf is binding by mere declaration (like manumission), since ownership is being removed. Muhammad requires delivery (taslim) to the administrator (mutawalli) and segregation (ifraz) and perpetuity (ta'bid). The reasoning is that dedicating to Allah is not a real transfer of ownership to Allah (since He already owns all), so it is akin to charity where delivery is needed. Muhammad cites an example: if one says 'This tree is for the mosque,' it does not become waqf without handing it over to the caretaker. The author then surveys the fatwa positions: Balkh scholars favor Abu Yusuf, al-Sadr al-Shahid and most regions favor Muhammad. Fath al-Qadir says Abu Yusuf's view is more appropriate for researchers, while al-Munya says the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf. The Bukharans adopt Muhammad. In al-Mabsut, Judge Abu Asim says Abu Yusuf is stronger rationally but Muhammad is closer to the practice of Umar. The refutation in al-Mabsut argues that Umar's placement of waqf with Hafsa was for management, not a condition for validity. Thus, the passage provides a comprehensive intra-Hanafi dispute on whether delivery is necessary for waqf completion.

Key Terms
القبض (al-qabd): Physical or constructive delivery of the waqf property to the trustee or beneficiary.
الإفراز (al-ifraz): Segregation of the waqf property from other properties, specifying it clearly.
التأبيد (al-ta'bid): Making the waqf perpetual, i.e., designating an ultimate charitable purpose that never ends.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, which of the following is required for the completion of waqf beyond the declaration?
A) Judicial decree
B) Delivery to the trustee and segregation
C) Registration with the government
D) Consent of all heirs

Key Takeaway
The necessity of delivery in waqf is a contested issue within the Hanafi school, with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad offering opposing analogies, leading to varied fatwa practices.

Waqf — Endowment

The Three Conditions for Binding Waqf: An Intra-Hanafi Analysis
Commentary on conditions for waqf binding—intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions required by Imam Muhammad for waqf to become binding and explain why Abu Yusuf disagrees, identifying the practical consequence (thamarah) of this ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Waqf becomes binding only upon delivery, separation, and perpetuity—Muhammad's view, but Abu Yusuf says mere utterance suffices.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over what completes a waqf. While all Hanafis agree that a waqf once binding is irrevocable, they differ on when it becomes binding. The matn states that waqf 'is not complete until it is taken possession, separated, and its end is made perpetual.' The commentator then unpacks this as the view of Imam Muhammad, contrasting it with Abu Yusuf's view that utterance alone suffices. This disagreement has real consequences for who controls the property before delivery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
From the first sentence, extract the three conditions Muhammad requires: qabd (delivery), ifraz (separation), ta'beed (perpetuity). Understand each term.
These conditions apply when the waqf is declared without a qadi's involvement.
2
Understand Abu Yusuf's counter-view
Abu Yusuf holds that utterance alone suffices, analogizing waqf to emancipation (i'tq). Both remove ownership, so the declaration is enough.
Abu Yusuf's view is based on qiyas with a similar shar'i act.
3
Examine Muhammad's dalil
Muhammad analogizes waqf to zakat and sadaqah: the right of Allah requires actual transfer. He also cites 'Umar's practice of placing his waqf in Hafsa's hand.
Muhammad's approach emphasizes the 'athar (tradition) over pure qiyas.
4
Trace the tarjih among later scholars
Note that Balkh scholars favor Abu Yusuf, Bukhara scholars favor Muhammad. Some say Abu Yusuf's view is easier and encourages waqf. Understand the basis of each preference.
This shows that later muftis selected views based on practical considerations.
5
Apply the dispute to the three derived masail
Work through the three scenarios: if the waqif tries to replace the trustee, Muhammad gives the trustee authority; Abu Yusuf gives the waqif authority. This illustrates the thamarah.
The practical outcome depends on which imam's view is followed.

فقهاء الأمصار أخذوا بقول محمد والفتوى عليه. وفي فتح القدير : وقول أبي يوسف أوجه عند المحققين. وفي المنية الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف. وهذا قول مشايخ بلخ، وأما البخاريون فأخذوا بقول محمد وفي المبسوط : كان القاضي أبو عاصم يقول: قول أبي يوسف من حيث المعنى أقوى إلا أنه قال: وقول محمد أقرب إلى موافقة الآثار يعني ما روي أن عمر رضي الله عنه جعل وقفه في يد حفصة وغير ذلك. ورده في المبسوط بأنه لا يلزم كونه ليتم الوقف بل لشغله وخوف التقصير إلى آخره. وفي البزازية : والإمام الثاني في قوله الأول ضيق ثم وسع كل التوسع حتى قال يتم بقوله وقفت ومشايخ قوله : (وقد مشى المؤلف أولا على قول أبي حنيفة قال في النهر : الأولى أن يحمل ما قاله أولاً  كتاب الوقف ۳۲۹ خوارزم أخذوا بقوله على ما حكاه نجم الزاهد في شرحه للمختصر ومحمد توسط وبقوله أخذ عامة المشايخ على ما حكاه في الفتاوي .اهـ. فالحاصل أن الترجيح قد اختلف والأخذ بقول أبي يوسف أحوط وأسهل ولذا قال في المحيط. ومشايخنا أخذوا بقول أبي يوسف ترغيباً للناس في الوقف. ويبتنى على هذا الخلاف مسائل : الأولى لو عزل الواقف القيم وأخرجه إلى غيره بلا شرط أن له ذلك قال محمد : لا ينعزل والولاية للقيم . الثانية لو مات وله وصي فلا ولاية لوصيه والولاية للقيم. الثالثة لو تولاه الواقف بنفسه لا يملك ذلك. وقال أبو يوسف: الولاية للواقف وله أن يعزل القيم في حياته ويولي غيره أو يرد النظر إلى نفسه، وإذا مات الواقف بطل ولاية القيم عنده لأنه بمنزلة وكيله، وأما إذا جعله قيماً في حياته وبعد موته فإنه لا ينعزل بموته اتفاقاً، وكذا لو شرط الولاية في عزل القوام والاستبدال لنفسه أو لأولاده وأخرجه من يده بهم وسلمه إلى المتولي فإنه جائز اتفاقاً نص عليه في السير الكبير لأن هذا شرط لا يخل بشرائط الواقف. وفي الخلاصة : إذا شرط الواقف أن يكون هو المتولي فعند أبي يوسف الوقف والشرط كلاهما صحيحان، وعند محمد وهلال الوقف والشرط باطلان .اهـ. وسيأتي آخر الباب ما يتعلق بالمتولي نصباً وتصرفاً.
His statement: (And it is not complete until it is taken possession, separated, and its end is made for a cause that does not cease) is an explanation of its special conditions according to the view of Muhammad. And the author first proceeded on the view of Abu Hanifa that it does not become binding except by judicial decree, and secondly on the conditions according to the view because the fatwa is on their view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that it becomes binding without judicial decree as we have presented. And when it becomes binding according to them, then according to Abu Yusuf it becomes binding by mere utterance, analogous to emancipation due to the commonality of removing ownership; Muhammad requires delivery to the trustee, separation, and perpetuation. As for the first, because the right of Allah the Exalted is established... [؟] Muhammad and it is not appropriate, and according to him it is within the delivery to the slave because making ownership for Allah the Exalted - and He is the owner of things - is not realized as an intended act, and it may be subsidiary to something else so it takes its ruling and is treated like zakat and charity. So if one says 'this tree is for the mosque', it does not become for it unless he delivers it to the caretaker of the mosque according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And in al-Khulasa: The scholars of Balkh give fatwa according to the view of Abu Yusuf, and al-Sadr al-Shahid said: The fatwa is according to the view of Muhammad. And in Sharh al-Majma': Most jurists of the regions adopted the view of Muhammad and the fatwa is upon it. And in Fath al-Qadir: The view of Abu Yusuf is more appropriate according to the verifiers. And in al-Munya: The fatwa is according to the view of Abu Yusuf. And this is the view of the scholars of Balkh. As for the Bukharans, they adopted the view of Muhammad. And in al-Mabsut: al-Qadi Abu Asim used to say: The view of Abu Yusuf is stronger in terms of meaning, except that he said: The view of Muhammad is closer to agreement with the athar, meaning what is narrated that Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) placed his waqf in the hand of Hafsa and other than that. And it was refuted in al-Mabsut by saying that it does not necessitate that it be to complete the waqf, but rather due to his occupation and fear of deficiency, etc. And in al-Bazzaziyya: And the second Imam (Abu Yusuf) in his first view was strict, then he expanded greatly until he said it is complete by saying 'I have endowed'. And the scholars of Khwarazm adopted his view according to what Najm al-Zahid narrated in his commentary on al-Mukhtasar. And Muhammad took a middle path, and the general body of scholars adopted his view according to what is narrated in al-Fatawa. The conclusion is that the preponderance has differed, and adopting the view of Abu Yusuf is more precautionary and easier. Therefore, it is said in al-Muhit: Our scholars adopted the view of Abu Yusuf to encourage people towards waqf. And upon this difference are built certain issues: First: If the waqif removes the trustee and appoints another without a condition that he has that right, Muhammad says: He is not removed and the authority is for the trustee. Second: If he dies and has an executor, the executor has no authority and the authority is for the trustee. Third: If the waqif undertakes it himself, he does not have that right. And Abu Yusuf says: The authority is for the waqif, and he may remove the trustee during his lifetime and appoint another or return the supervision to himself. And when the waqif dies, the authority of the trustee becomes void according to him because he is like his agent. But if he made him a trustee during his life and after his death, then he is not removed by his death by agreement. Similarly, if he stipulated authority in removing trustees and replacing for himself or his children, and removed it from his hand and handed it over to the trustee, then it is permissible by agreement as stated in al-Siyar al-Kabir, because this condition does not violate the conditions of the waqif. And in al-Khulasa: If the waqif stipulates that he himself be the trustee, then according to Abu Yusuf both the waqf and the condition are valid; according to Muhammad and Hilal, both the waqf and the condition are void. And the end of the chapter will discuss what relates to the trustee in terms of appointment and disposition.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn condition for the completion of waqf. It opens by identifying the three conditions required according to Imam Muhammad: qabd (delivery), ifraz (separation), and ta'beed (perpetuity). The commentator notes that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq initially followed Abu Hanifa's view that waqf is not binding except by a qadi's ruling, then later followed Muhammad's conditions because the fatwa is on the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that waqf becomes binding without a qadi. The passage then details the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf likens waqf to emancipation—both remove ownership—so utterance alone suffices; Muhammad requires delivery because the right of Allah is established through actual transfer, analogous to zakat and sadaqah. The text then surveys later authorities' tarjih: some prefer Abu Yusuf for ease, others Muhammad for following the practice of the Companions. Three derived masail show the practical consequence: if the waqif tries to replace the trustee, Muhammad gives the trustee authority; Abu Yusuf gives the waqif authority. The passage ends by deferring further discussion of the trustee.

Key Terms
القبض (al-qabd): Delivery or taking possession of the waqf property by the trustee (mutawalli). Required by Muhammad for completion of waqf.
الإفراز (al-ifraz): Separation of the waqf property from the waqif's ownership, e.g., by identifying a specific portion in a shared property.
التأبيد (al-ta'beed): Making the waqf perpetual, meaning the ultimate destination (e.g., the poor, a mosque) must be a continuing cause that cannot end.
المتولي (al-mutawalli): The trustee or administrator of the waqf property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding trustee removal?
A) Muhammad allows the waqif to remove the trustee freely; Abu Yusuf does not.
B) Abu Yusuf allows the waqif to remove the trustee and appoint another or take over; Muhammad gives the trustee authority and does not allow removal.
C) Both agree that the waqif cannot remove the trustee after delivery.
D) Abu Yusuf requires a qadi to approve removal; Muhammad allows removal by the waqif.

Key Takeaway
A waqf becomes binding upon delivery, separation, and perpetuity according to Imam Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf holds that utterance alone suffices—a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with practical differences for trustee authority.

Validity of Waqf Musha' (Undivided Share)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waqf musha'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on waqf of an undivided share, explain the basis in the dispute about qabd (delivery), and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Waqf of an undivided share in divisible property is invalid – the fatwa follows Imam Muhammad requiring separation.

The validity of endowing an undivided share (musha') depends on whether the endowment requires separation (ifraz) of the share. This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf, its basis in the earlier dispute about delivery (qabd), and the practical rule for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Note that Imam Muhammad holds waqf musha' invalid for divisible property, while Imam Abu Yusuf holds it valid. The difference stems from their respective conditions for a valid waqf.
The text states: 'فلا يجوز وقف المشاع' for Muhammad, and 'هو جائز' for Abu Yusuf.
2
Understand the basis in qabd
The dispute is built on the earlier condition of qabd (delivery). Those who require qabd also require ifraz (separation) – thus musha' is invalid. Those who do not require qabd permit musha'.
'وهو مبني على الشرط الأول لأن القسمة من تمام القبض'
3
Note the exceptions
For indivisible property (e.g., a small well), waqf musha' is valid by agreement. However, for mosques and cemeteries, it is invalid even if indivisible due to the need for exclusive use.
Except: مسجد ومقبرة – they cannot be shared.
4
Identify the fatwa hierarchy
Later Hanafi authorities (al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, etc.) state that the fatwa is on Muhammad's view. This is the relied-upon position for practice.
Al-Khulasa: 'الفتوى على قول محمد'

وأما الثاني أعني اشتراط الإفراز فقد علمت أنه قول محمد فلا يجوز وقف المشاع. وقال أبو يوسف : هو جائز وهو مبني على الشرط الأول لأن القسمة من تمام القبض فمن شرطه لم يجوز وقف المشاع ومن لم يشترطه جوزه والخلاف فيما يحتمل القسمة، أما ما لا يحتمل القسمة فهو جائز اتفاقاً اعتباراً عند محمد بالهبة والصدقة المنفذة إلا في المسجد والمقبرة فإنه لا يتم مع الشيوع فيما لا يحتمل القسمة عند أبي يوسف أيضاً لأن بقاء الشركة يمنع الخلوص لله تعالى ولأن المهايأة في هذا في غاية القبح بأن يقبر فيها الموتى سنة وتززع سنة ويصلى الله فيه في وقت ويتخذ إصطبلاً في وقت بخلاف الوقف لإمكان الاستغلال. والحاصل أن وقف المشاع مسجداً أو مقبرة غير جائز مطلقاً اتفاقاً، وفي غيرهما إن كان مما لا يحتمل القسمة جاز اتفاقاً. والخلاف فيما يحتملها، ومن أخذ بقول أبي يوسف في خروجه بمجرد مشايخ بلخ أخذ بقوله في هذه، ومن أخذ بقول محمد في القبض وهو مشايخ بخارى أخذ بقوله في وقف المشاع. وصرح في الخلاصة من الإجارة والوقف بأن الفتوى على قول محمد في وقف المشاع وكذا في البزازية والولوالجية وشرح المجمع لابن الملك. وفي التجنيس : وبقوله يفتى. وتبعه في غاية البيان وسيأتي بيان ما إذا قضى بجوازه . وفي ا الخلاصة : وإذا وقف أحد الشريكين نصيبه المشاع على قول أبي يوسف ثم اقتسما فوقع نصيب الواقف في موضع لا يجب عليه أن يقفه ثانياً لأن القسمة تعين الموقوف، وإذا أراد الاجتناب عن على بيان مسألة إجماعية هي أن الملك بالقضاء يزول، أما إذا خلا عن القضاء فلا يزول إلا بعد هذه الشروط عند محمد واختاره المصنف تبعاً لعامة المشايخ . قوله : (وقال أبو يوسف الولاية للواقف الخ) اللفظ وهم الخلاف
As for the second, meaning the condition of separation (ifraz), you know that it is the view of Muhammad, so waqf of an undivided share (musha') is not permissible. And Abu Yusuf said: It is permissible, and it is based on the first condition because division is part of delivery. So whoever stipulates it does not permit waqf of musha', and whoever does not stipulate it permits it. And the difference is in what can be divided. As for what cannot be divided, it is permissible by agreement, according to Muhammad by analogy with the executed gift and charity, except in the case of a mosque and a cemetery, because it is not complete with common ownership even in what cannot be divided according to Abu Yusuf as well, because the continuation of partnership prevents exclusivity for Allah the Exalted, and because the alternation (muhaaya'a) in this is extremely ugly—such as burying the dead in it one year, planting it another year, praying in it at one time, and making it a stable at another time—unlike [other] waqf where exploitation is possible. The conclusion is that waqf of an undivided share as a mosque or cemetery is absolutely impermissible by agreement. In other than these, if it is something that cannot be divided, it is permissible by agreement. The difference is in what can be divided. And whoever adopts the view of Abu Yusuf in its completion by mere utterance—the scholars of Balkh adopt his view in this. And whoever adopts the view of Muhammad regarding delivery—the scholars of Bukhara adopt his view in waqf musha'. And it is stated explicitly in al-Khulasa from the chapter of Ijara and Waqf that the fatwa is according to the view of Muhammad in waqf musha', and similarly in al-Bazzaziyya, al-Walawaljiyya, and Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malik. And in al-Tajnis: And by his view fatwa is given. And followed by Ghayat al-Bayan. And there will come an explanation of when a qadi rules on its permissibility. And in al-Khulasa: If one of the partners endows his undivided share according to the view of Abu Yusuf, and then they partition, and the share of the waqif falls in a location, he is not required to waqf it a second time because the partition specifies the endowed property. And if he wishes to avoid ... [؟] on an explanation of a consensual issue that ownership is removed by judicial decree, but if there is no judicial decree, it is not removed except after these conditions according to Muhammad, and the author chose it following the general body of scholars. His statement: (And Abu Yusuf said: The authority belongs to the waqif...) the wording [؟] and the difference.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the second condition for waqf: ifraz (separation). It states that according to Muhammad, ifraz is required, therefore waqf of an undivided share (musha') in a divisible property is invalid. Abu Yusuf, who does not require ifraz, holds that waqf musha' is valid. The ruling depends on the earlier dispute about qabd: those who require qabd (Muhammad) also require ifraz, so musha' is invalid; those who do not require qabd (Abu Yusuf) permit musha'. An exception is made for properties that cannot be divided, such as a small well or bath: these are valid by agreement, except for mosques and cemeteries, where musha' is invalid even if indivisible, because shared use is not appropriate for these sacred purposes. The text then aligns the geographical preferences: Balkh follows Abu Yusuf (permit musha'), Bukhara follows Muhammad (prohibit musha'). Later authorities like al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, etc., state that the fatwa is on Muhammad's view, prohibiting musha' in divisible properties. A practical consequence: if someone endows his undivided share according to Abu Yusuf's view, and later the property is partitioned, the endowed share is specified by the partition and no new endowment is needed. The passage ends with a note that ownership is only removed by qadi's decree, or by fulfilling the conditions according to Muhammad.

Key Terms
المشاع (al-musha'): An undivided share in a jointly owned property. The text discusses waqf of such a share.
الإفراز (al-ifraz): Separation or partition of a share from the jointly owned property. Required by Imam Muhammad for a valid waqf of a share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, is the waqf of an undivided share (musha') in a divisible property valid?
A) Yes, it is valid.
B) No, it is invalid.
C) It depends on the qadi's ruling.
D) It is valid only if the property is a mosque.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa on waqf musha' follows Imam Muhammad: an undivided share in a divisible property cannot be endowed unless first separated; exceptions apply for indivisible (non-sacred) properties.

Dispute on the Waqif's Authority Over the Mutawalli
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waqif's authority over mutawalli

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the waqif's authority to dismiss the mutawalli, and explain the practical consequences of their disagreement.

Core Idea
The waqif's authority to dismiss the mutawalli is disputed: Muhammad says no, Abu Yusuf says yes.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf on whether the waqif retains authority to dismiss the mutawalli (qayyim) and take over management. The core of the disagreement lies in the legal characterization of the mutawalli's appointment: is he like an independent executor or a revocable agent? This lesson will guide you through the two positions, their analogical foundations, and the practical consequences that follow.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the precise question: can the waqif dismiss the mutawalli (qayyim) without having stipulated that right in the waqf deed?
2
Identify the positions
State the view of Muhammad: the mutawalli is not dismissed and retains authority. State the view of Abu Yusuf: the waqif has full authority to dismiss, replace, or take over.
3
Examine the analogical basis
Muhammad compares the mutawalli to an executor (wasi) who has independent authority; Abu Yusuf compares him to an agent (wakil) who is subject to the principal's control. Understand how this analogy drives the ruling.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Work through the three scenarios given: (a) waqif dismisses mutawalli, (b) waqif dies leaving an executor, (c) waqif wants to take over personally. Determine the ruling under each view.
5
Note the tarjih and practice
Observe that the text does not give a definitive tarjih but notes that many later scholars favored Abu Yusuf's view for practical ease. See how the dispute influences fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبتنى على هذا الخلاف مسائل : الأولى لو عزل الواقف القيم وأخرجه إلى غيره بلا شرط أن له ذلك قال محمد : لا ينعزل والولاية للقيم . الثانية لو مات وله وصي فلا ولاية لوصيه والولاية للقيم. الثالثة لو تولاه الواقف بنفسه لا يملك ذلك. وقال أبو يوسف: الولاية للواقف وله أن يعزل القيم في حياته ويولي غيره أو يرد النظر إلى نفسه، وإذا مات الواقف بطل ولاية القيم عنده لأنه بمنزلة وكيله، وأما إذا جعله قيماً في حياته وبعد موته فإنه لا ينعزل بموته اتفاقاً، وكذا لو شرط الولاية في عزل القوام والاستبدال لنفسه أو لأولاده وأخرجه من يده بهم وسلمه إلى المتولي فإنه جائز اتفاقاً نص عليه في السير الكبير لأن هذا شرط لا يخل بشرائط الواقف. وفي الخلاصة : إذا شرط الواقف أن يكون هو المتولي فعند أبي يوسف الوقف والشرط كلاهما صحيحان، وعند محمد وهلال الوقف والشرط باطلان .اهـ. وسيأتي آخر الباب ما يتعلق بالمتولي نصباً وتصرفاً. قوله : (وقال أبو يوسف الولاية للواقف الخ) اللفظ وهم الخلاف
And based on this difference are issues: First, if the waqif dismisses the mutawalli and removes him to another without stipulating that he has that right, Muhammad said: He is not dismissed and authority remains with the mutawalli. Second, if [the waqif] dies and has an executor, the executor has no authority and authority remains with the mutawalli. Third, if the waqif takes over himself, he does not own that. Abu Yusuf said: Authority belongs to the waqif, and he may dismiss the mutawalli during his lifetime and appoint another or return the management to himself. When the waqif dies, the mutawalli's authority becomes void according to him because he is like his agent. But if he made him a mutawalli during his life and after his death, he is not dismissed by his death by agreement. Similarly, if he stipulated authority in dismissing mutawallis and making replacements for himself or his children and removed it from his hand and delivered it to the trustee, that is permissible by agreement as stated in al-Siyar al-Kabir because this stipulation does not violate the waqif's conditions. In al-Khulasa: If the waqif stipulates that he himself be the trustee, according to Abu Yusuf both the waqf and the stipulation are valid; according to Muhammad and Hilal both are invalid. And will come at the end of the chapter what pertains to the trustee appointment and actions. His statement: (And Abu Yusuf said authority is for the waqif etc.) the wording and delusion of difference.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the waqif's authority over the mutawalli (qayyim). The dispute arises from the legal nature of the mutawalli's position. Muhammad considers the mutawalli as having an independent right once appointed, analogous to an executor (wasi), and thus the waqif cannot dismiss him or take over management. Abu Yusuf, however, views the mutawalli as the waqif's agent (wakil), so the waqif retains full authority to dismiss, replace, or assume management himself. The text lists three practical consequences: (1) If the waqif dismisses the mutawalli without prior stipulation, Muhammad holds the dismissal ineffective; (2) if the waqif dies, his executor does not inherit authority over the waqf according to Muhammad; (3) the waqif cannot take over personally. Then Abu Yusuf's counterposition is given, emphasizing the waqif's ongoing control. An additional citation from al-Khulasa notes that if the waqif stipulates himself as mutawalli, Abu Yusuf validates both waqf and condition, while Muhammad and Hilal invalidate both. The note at the end likely refers to a textual variant but is unclear. The passage is from a commentary expanding on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Key Terms
القيم (al-qayyim): The mutawalli or administrator of a waqf, appointed by the waqif.
الولاية (al-wilayah): The authority or legal power to manage the waqf property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, if a waqif dismisses the mutawalli without having stipulated the right to do so, what happens?
A) The mutawalli is dismissed and the waqif takes over.
B) The mutawalli is not dismissed and remains in authority.
C) The dismissal is valid only if approved by a judge.
D) The waqf becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The waqif's authority to dismiss a mutawalli without stipulation is a contested issue within the Hanafi school, with Muhammad opposing dismissal and Abu Yusuf permitting it.

Waqf of Musha' (Undivided Share): The Core Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of waqf of undivided share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on waqf of musha' and explain the basis for the relied-upon position (Muhammad's view).

Core Idea
Waqf of an undivided share is invalid per the fatwa; delivery and separation are conditions for Muhammad.

This lesson addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: is waqf of an undivided share (musha') valid? The answer depends on whether delivery (qabd) is a condition for waqf. We examine the conflicting views of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf, and see why the fatwa ultimately sides with Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Identify the views of Muhammad (invalid) and Abu Yusuf (valid) regarding waqf of musha' in divisible property.
Both are within the Hanafi school; the dispute is on the condition of delivery.
2
Identify the root cause
The dispute is based on whether delivery (qabd) is a condition for the validity of waqf. Muhammad requires it; Abu Yusuf does not.
Muhammad analogizes to gift and charity; Abu Yusuf views waqf as complete upon declaration.
3
Analyze the consensus cases
For property not capable of division, waqf of musha' is valid by consensus. Exception: mosques and cemeteries are invalid by consensus even if indivisible.
This shows the rule is not absolute.
4
Identify the fatwa (mufta bihi)
The later jurists (e.g., al-Khulasa, al-Bazaziyya) state that the fatwa is on Muhammad's view: waqf of musha' in divisible property is invalid.
This is the operative ruling for practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a person cannot make a waqf of a half-share of a divisible house; it would be invalid. If the property is indivisible, it is valid (except mosque/cemetery).
This distinction is essential for fatwa-giving.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني أعني اشتراط الإفراز فقد علمت أنه قول محمد فلا يجوز وقف المشاع. وقال أبو يوسف : هو جائز وهو مبني على الشرط الأول لأن القسمة من تمام القبض فمن شرطه لم يجوز وقف المشاع ومن لم يشترطه جوزه والخلاف فيما يحتمل القسمة، أما ما لا يحتمل القسمة فهو جائز اتفاقاً اعتباراً عند محمد بالهبة والصدقة المنفذة إلا في المسجد والمقبرة فإنه لا يتم مع الشيوع فيما لا يحتمل القسمة عند أبي يوسف أيضاً لأن بقاء الشركة يمنع الخلوص لله تعالى ولأن المهايأة في هذا في غاية القبح بأن يقبر فيها الموتى سنة وتززع سنة ويصلى الله فيه في وقت ويتخذ إصطبلاً في وقت بخلاف الوقف لإمكان الاستغلال. والحاصل أن وقف المشاع مسجداً أو مقبرة غير جائز مطلقاً اتفاقاً، وفي غيرهما إن كان مما لا يحتمل القسمة جاز اتفاقاً. والخلاف فيما يحتملها، ومن أخذ بقول أبي يوسف في خروجه بمجرد مشايخ بلخ أخذ بقوله في هذه، ومن أخذ بقول محمد في القبض وهو مشايخ بخارى أخذ بقوله في وقف المشاع. وصرح في الخلاصة من الإجارة والوقف بأن الفتوى على قول محمد في وقف المشاع وكذا في البزازية والولوالجية وشرح المجمع لابن الملك. وفي التجنيس : وبقوله يفتى. وتبعه في غاية البيان وسيأتي بيان ما إذا قضى بجوازه . وفي الخلاصة : وإذا وقف أحد الشريكين نصيبه المشاع على قول أبي يوسف ثم اقتسما فوقع نصيب الواقف في موضع لا يجب عليه أن يقفه ثانياً لأن القسمة تعين الموقوف، وإذا أراد الاجتناب عن على بيان مسألة إجماعية هي أن الملك بالقضاء يزول، أما إذا خلا عن القضاء فلا يزول إلا بعد هذه الشروط عند محمد واختاره المصنف تبعاً لعامة المشايخ . ثم قال : يبيع يقف المقسوم ثانياً، ولو كان الأرض له فوقف نصفها ثم أراد القسمة فالوجه في ذلك أن . ما بقي ثم يقتسمان، وإن لم يبع ورفع إلى القاضي ليأمر إنساناً بالقسمة معه جاز؛ كذا الخلاصة أيضاً. وفيها : حانوت بين اثنين وقف أحدهما نصيبه وأراد أن يضرب لوح الوقف على بابه فمنعه الشريك الآخر ليس له الضرب إلا إذا أمره القاضي بذلك وهذا قول أبي يوسف، أما على قول محمد فلا يتأتى هذا. وفي الظهيرية ولو كانت له أرضون ودور بينه وبين آخر فوقف نصيبه ثم أراد أن يقاسم شريكه ويجمع الوقف كله في أرض واحدة ودار واحدة فإنه جائز في قياس قول أبي يوسف وهلال، وإذا قاسم الواقف شريكه وبينهما دراهم فإن كان الواقف هو الذي أعطى الدراهم جاز لأنه في حصة الوقف قاسم شریکه واشترى أيضاً ما لم يقف من نصيب شريكه فجاز ذلك كله، ثم حصة الوقف للواقف وما اشتراه بالدراهم فذلك له وليس بوقف اهـ. ولو وقف جميع أرضه ثم استحق جزء منه بطل في الباقي عند محمد لأن الشيوع مقارن كما في الهبة بخلاف ما إذا رجع الواهب في البعض أو رجع الوارث في الثلثين بعد موت المريض وقد وهب أو وقف في مرضه وفي المال ضيق لأن الشيوع في ذلك طار، ولو استحق جزء مميز بعينه لم يبطل في الباقي لعدم الشيوع ولهذا جاز في الابتداء، وعلى هذا الهبة والصدقة المملوكة ؛ كذا في الهداية ولو كانت الأرض بين رجلين فوقفاها على بعض الوجوه ودفعاها إلى وال يقوم عليها كان ذلك جائزاً عند محمد لأن المانع من تمام الصدقة شيوع في المحل المتصدق به ولا شيوع هنا لأن الكل صدقة. غاية الأمر أن ذلك مع كثرة المتصدقين والقبض من الوالي في الكل وجد جملة واحدة فهو كما لو تصدق بها رجل واحد بخلاف ما لو وقف كل منهما نصفها شائعاً على حدة وجعل لها والياً على حدة لا يجوز لأنهما صدقتان، ولو وقف كل منهما نصيبه وجعلا الوالي فسلماها إليه جميعاً جاز لأن تمامها بالقبض والقبض يجتمع ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. والمشاع غير المقسوم من شاع يشيع شيعاً وشيوعاً ومشاعاً؛ كذا في القاموس.
As for the second [condition], namely the stipulation of separation, you know that it is the view of Muhammad, so waqf of undivided property is not valid. Abu Yusuf said: It is permissible, and it is based on the first condition because division is part of delivery; whoever stipulates it does not permit waqf of undivided property, and whoever does not stipulate it permits it. The dispute concerns what is capable of division. As for what is not capable of division, it is valid by consensus, by analogy according to Muhammad with gift and direct alms, except for a mosque and cemetery, for it is not completed with common ownership even in what is not capable of division according to Abu Yusuf as well, because remaining partnership prevents exclusivity for Allah, and because alternating use in this is extremely repugnant—burying dead one year and planting the next, praying in it at one time and using it as a stable at another—unlike waqf because exploitation is possible. The conclusion: waqf of undivided property as a mosque or cemetery is absolutely invalid by consensus; in other cases, if it is not capable of division, it is valid by consensus. The dispute is over what is capable of division. Whoever takes Abu Yusuf's view in its issuance alone, the mashayikh of Balkh take his view in this; whoever takes Muhammad's view on delivery, the mashayikh of Bukhara take his view on waqf of undivided property. In al-Khulasa from Kitab al-Ijara and al-Waqf it is stated that the fatwa is on Muhammad's view regarding waqf of undivided property, and similarly in al-Bazaziyya, al-Walwalijiyya, and Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malik. In al-Tajnis: And by his view fatwa is given. And Ghayat al-Bayan followed him, and the explanation of when a judge rules its permissibility will come. In al-Khulasa: If one of two partners waqf his undivided share according to Abu Yusuf's view and then they divide, and the waqif's share falls in a place, he is not required to make it waqf again because division specifies the waqf property. And if he wants to avoid… the explanation of a consensual issue that ownership ceases by judicial decree, but if devoid of decree, it does not cease except after these conditions according to Muhammad, and the author chose this following the majority of mashayikh. Then he said: He sells and then makes the divided property waqf again. If the land was his and he waqf half of it then wants division, the way in that is… what remains then they divide. If he does not sell and raises it to the judge to order someone to divide with him, it is permissible; likewise in al-Khulasa. In it: A shop between two, one of them waqf his share and wants to affix the waqf plate on his door, the other partner prevents him; he may not affix unless the judge orders him, and this is Abu Yusuf's view; as for Muhammad's view, this cannot happen. In al-Zahiriyya: If he owned lands and houses in common with another, and waqf his share, then wants to partition with his partner and gather all the waqf in one land and one house, it is permissible according to the analogue of Abu Yusuf and Hilal. If the waqif partitions with his partner and there are dirhams between them, if the waqif is the one who gave the dirhams, it is permissible because in the waqf share he has divided with his partner and also purchased what was not waqf from his partner's share, so all that is permissible. Then the waqf share is for the waqif, and what he bought with the dirhams is his, not waqf. If he waqf all his land then part is claimed successfully, it becomes void in the rest according to Muhammad because the common ownership is concurrent, as in a gift, unlike if the donor retracts part, or the heir retracts two-thirds after the patient's death and he had given a gift or waqf while ill and the estate is constrained, because common ownership in that is supervening. If a specifically identified part is claimed successfully, it does not void the rest due to lack of common ownership, and thus it is permissible initially. And on this is gift and owned charity; as in al-Hidaya. If the land was between two men and they both waqf it for some purposes and deliver it to a guardian to manage it, that is permissible according to Muhammad because the preventer of completion of charity is common ownership in the subject of charity, and there is no common ownership here because all is charity. Except that, with many donors and the guardian taking possession of all at once, it is as if one man gave it as charity, unlike if each of them waqfd his half separately and appointed a separate guardian, that is not permissible because they are two charities. If each waqfd his share and they appointed one guardian and delivered both to him together, it is permissible because completion is by possession and possession can combine; as in Fath al-Qadir. Undivided property that is not partitioned: from sha'a yashi'u shay'aan wa shuyu'an wa musha'an; as in al-Qamus.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of waqf of an undivided share (musha') in property. The dispute is based on whether the delivery of possession (qabd) is a condition for the validity of waqf. Muhammad holds that delivery is necessary and that it requires separation (ifraz) of the waqf property from the owner's other property; thus waqf of an undivided share is invalid because separation is impossible while the share remains undivided. Abu Yusuf, on the other hand, does not require delivery as a condition for the validity of waqf; the waqf is complete upon the declaration, so waqf of an undivided share is permissible. The text explains that where division is impossible (e.g., a very small piece of land), both agree it is valid, except for mosques and cemeteries which are unanimously invalid as musha' due to the impossibility of exclusive dedication to Allah. The fatwa is stated to be on Muhammad's view, according to the authors of al-Khulasa, al-Bazaziyya, al-Walwalijiyya, and others. The passage then details various practical applications: if one partner waqfs his share on Abu Yusuf's view and then they partition, the waqf property is specified; if the waqif wants to affix a sign, he needs judicial permission on Abu Yusuf's view; combining waqfs from multiple donors into one administration is permissible if done collectively. It also discusses the effect of a successful claim (istihqaq) on part of the waqf property: if the part claimed is undifferentiated, the entire waqf is voided according to Muhammad (due to concurrent common ownership), but if it is a specific part, only that part is voided. The passage ends with a lexical definition of 'musha'.

Key Terms
المشاع (al-musha'): Undivided property; a share in common ownership that is not separated from the whole.
الإفراز (al-ifraz): The separation or partition of a share from the joint property, making it distinct.
القبض (al-qabd): Taking possession or delivery of the waqf property, considered by Muhammad as necessary for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on waqf of an undivided share (musha') in a house that can be easily partitioned?
A) Valid by consensus.
B) Valid according to Abu Yusuf but invalid according to others.
C) Invalid according to the relied-upon view.
D) Valid only if the waqif is also the mutawalli.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that waqf of an undivided share (musha') in divisible property is invalid, based on Muhammad's requirement of delivery and separation.

Waqf — Endowment

Waqf of Musha': Practical Applications and Subsidiary Rulings
Expansion of waqf musha' rulings into practical applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling on waqf of musha' to scenarios involving partition, judicial action, and successful claims (istihqaq).

Core Idea
Even if waqf of musha' is invalid per the fatwa, certain practical arrangements—like collective waqf or judicial partition—can achieve a valid result.

This lesson extends the dispute on waqf of musha' into practical scenarios: what if partners waqf together, or a judge intervenes? We explore the detailed fatwas from later Hanafi works on partition, combination, and the effect of a successful claim on part of the property.

Guided Path
1
Understand the consensus exceptions
Waqf of musha' in indivisible property is valid by consensus, except mosques/cemeteries. This is the baseline for practical cases.
2
Apply the fatwa to partition scenarios
If one partner waqfs his share on Abu Yusuf's view and then they partition, the waqf becomes specified and valid. If the waqif wants to affix a waqf sign, he needs judicial permission on Abu Yusuf's view.
These are practical implications of the difference.
3
Analyze collective waqf
If both partners waqf their shares together to a single guardian, it is permissible per Muhammad because there is no common ownership among donors. If each waqfs separately with separate guardians, it is invalid.
The key is unity of transaction and possession.
4
Examine the effect of istihqaq
If a successful claim is made on an undifferentiated part of the waqf property, the entire waqf is voided per Muhammad (concurrent common ownership). If the claimed part is specifically identified, only that part is voided.
This is a subsidiary intra-Hanafi dispute.
5
Consider judicial intervention
The judge can order division or allow the waqf plate. If a judge rules per Abu Yusuf, the waqf becomes effective judicially, but the fatwa remains on Muhammad.
Judicial decree does not change the underlying rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

والخلاف فيما يحتمل القسمة، أما ما لا يحتمل القسمة فهو جائز اتفاقاً اعتباراً عند محمد بالهبة والصدقة المنفذة إلا في المسجد والمقبرة فإنه لا يتم مع الشيوع فيما لا يحتمل القسمة عند أبي يوسف أيضاً لأن بقاء الشركة يمنع الخلوص لله تعالى ولأن المهايأة في هذا في غاية القبح بأن يقبر فيها الموتى سنة وتززع سنة ويصلى الله فيه في وقت ويتخذ إصطبلاً في وقت بخلاف الوقف لإمكان الاستغلال. والحاصل أن وقف المشاع القبض وهو مشايخ بخارى أخذ بقوله في وقف المشاع. وصرح في الخلاصة من الإجارة والوقف بأن الفتوى على قول محمد في وقف المشاع وكذا في البزازية والولوالجية وشرح المجمع لابن الملك. وفي التجنيس : وبقوله يفتى. وتبعه في غاية البيان وسيأتي بيان ما إذا قضى بجوازه . وفي الخلاصة : وإذا وقف أحد الشريكين نصيبه المشاع على قول أبي يوسف ثم اقتسما فوقع نصيب الواقف في موضع لا يجب عليه أن يقفه ثانياً لأن القسمة تعين الموقوف، وإذا أراد الاجتناب عن على بيان مسألة إجماعية هي أن الملك بالقضاء يزول، أما إذا خلا عن القضاء فلا يزول إلا بعد هذه الشروط عند محمد واختاره المصنف تبعاً لعامة المشايخ . ثم قال : يبيع يقف المقسوم ثانياً، ولو كان الأرض له فوقف نصفها ثم أراد القسمة فالوجه في ذلك أن . ما بقي ثم يقتسمان، وإن لم يبع ورفع إلى القاضي ليأمر إنساناً بالقسمة معه جاز؛ كذا الخلاصة أيضاً. وفيها : حانوت بين اثنين وقف أحدهما نصيبه وأراد أن يضرب لوح الوقف على بابه فمنعه الشريك الآخر ليس له الضرب إلا إذا أمره القاضي بذلك وهذا قول أبي يوسف، أما على قول محمد فلا يتأتى هذا. وفي الظهيرية ولو كانت له أرضون ودور بينه وبين آخر فوقف نصيبه ثم أراد أن يقاسم شريكه ويجمع الوقف كله في أرض واحدة ودار واحدة فإنه جائز في قياس قول أبي يوسف وهلال، وإذا قاسم الواقف شريكه وبينهما دراهم فإن كان الواقف هو الذي أعطى الدراهم جاز لأنه في حصة الوقف قاسم شریکه واشترى أيضاً ما لم يقف من نصيب شريكه فجاز ذلك كله، ثم حصة الوقف للواقف وما اشتراه بالدراهم فذلك له وليس بوقف اهـ. ولو وقف جميع أرضه ثم استحق جزء منه بطل في الباقي عند محمد الباقي لعدم الشيوع ولهذا جاز في الابتداء، وعلى هذا الهبة والصدقة المملوكة ؛ كذا في الهداية ولو كانت الأرض بين رجلين فوقفاها على بعض الوجوه ودفعاها إلى وال يقوم عليها كان ذلك جائزاً عند محمد لأن المانع من تمام الصدقة شيوع في المحل المتصدق به ولا شيوع هنا لأن الكل صدقة. غاية الأمر أن ذلك مع كثرة المتصدقين والقبض من الوالي في الكل وجد جملة واحدة فهو كما لو تصدق بها رجل واحد بخلاف ما لو وقف كل منهما نصفها شائعاً على حدة وجعل لها والياً على حدة لا يجوز لأنهما صدقتان، ولو وقف كل منهما نصيبه وجعلا الوالي فسلماها إليه جميعاً جاز لأن تمامها بالقبض والقبض يجتمع ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. والمشاع غير المقسوم
